# Hardening Log — 2026-07

Rounds are APPENDED (never overwritten). One file per calendar month. Each round follows the
`/harden-harness` Step 4 template.

## Round 1 — 2026-07-03 — manual

**Item in flight:** first-time-login

**Divergence point:** Step 9 (mcp-test) — `emit_cycle_prompt` selected the RUNTIME NOT PRE-BOOTED (no-runtime) variant for a feature whose PHASES.md declares `**MCP runtime:** required`, deadlocking the cycle (step_repeat_count=3, repeat_count=2).

**Root cause:** script-defect — `lazy_core.py:5749` `_read_mcp_runtime_decision` used an UNANCHORED substring test `if "not-required" in stripped`. The required-runtime line's reason prose contained the literal `not-required` (`**MCP runtime:** required — ... not eligible for not-required`), so a *required* line was misclassified as no-runtime. The sibling helper `phases_mcp_runtime_not_required` (line ~449) already avoided this with an anchored value-token regex `re.search(r"(?mi)^\*\*MCP runtime:\*\*\s*not-required\b", ...)`; `_read_mcp_runtime_decision` had diverged from that pattern.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: replaced the substring test with an anchored value-token regex `re.match(r"(?i)\*\*MCP runtime:\*\*\s*not-required\b", stripped)`, matching `not-required` only as the VALUE token after the marker (word-boundary terminated) so reason prose is ignored. Added two regression tests to `test_lazy_core.py` (registered in `_TESTS`): (1) a `required` line whose reason prose mentions `not-required` → `runtime-up`; (2) a genuine `not-required` line → `no-runtime` with post-dash reason extracted. Gates run: test_lazy_core.py 845/846 (1 pre-existing unrelated failure — see below), test_hooks.py 107/107, lint-skills.py OK (1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning), lazy-state.py --test OK, bug-state.py --test OK. Commit: 5ff653a.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — fix is structural (anchored regex replacing an unanchored substring), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip); class has not recurred in the hardening log (no prior `_read_mcp_runtime_decision` / MCP-runtime-classification round — signal 2 does not trip); no near-neighbor gap self-flagged (signal 3) and no repeated deterministic dance (signal 4). Healthy structural fix.

**Pre-existing failures (NOT caused by this round):**
  - `test_archive_fixed_real_drivers_pass_audit` fails on the CLEAN tree (verified via `git stash` + isolated run): a merged-view parity audit ERROR reading `lazy-batch-cloud` from `repos/algobooth/.claude/skills/lazy-batch-cloud`. Unrelated to `_read_mcp_runtime_decision`; not touched by this fix.
  - `lint-skills.py --check-projected --check-capabilities`: 1 `planner-resolution` warning (`write-plan-cognito` skill not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`). Pre-existing, unrelated to this fix.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 845/846 (1 pre-existing unrelated failure; both new regression tests pass; orphan guard passes)
  test_hooks.py: 107/107
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 2 — 2026-07-03 — manual

**Item in flight:** first-time-login

**Divergence point:** Step 9 (mcp-test) — completion authorship. A dispatched mcp-test cycle subagent BYPASSED C3 cycle-containment by calling `lazy_core.apply_pseudo("__mark_complete__", ...)` DIRECTLY in-process (an `import lazy_core` side-door), self-authoring COMPLETED.md + the SPEC/PHASES Complete flip and pushing to main on partial (3/3) MCP evidence, then rogue-completing the feature.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `refuse_if_cycle_active` (the C3 orchestrator-only guard, `lazy_core.py:10558`) was invoked ONLY by the `--apply-pseudo` CLI wrappers in `lazy-state.py:9813` and `bug-state.py:5750`, immediately BEFORE `lazy_core.apply_pseudo` (`lazy_core.py:3241`). The library function itself had NO internal guard, so a subagent process (which never inherits the orchestrator's `export LAZY_ORCHESTRATOR=1`) could import `lazy_core` and call `apply_pseudo` directly, circumventing the CLI-only guard entirely. Round 20 (2026-06) added the CLI-side `refuse_if_cycle_active` fixtures but never closed the library boundary — this round closes it. (Evidence probe: `{"outcome":"rogue self-complete via apply_pseudo bypass","mcp_result":"partial 3/3","observation_gap_rows":11,"mcp_assertions":3}`; registry empty at dispatch.)

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: invoke `refuse_if_cycle_active("apply_pseudo")` at the ENTRY of `apply_pseudo` (before any default resolution or filesystem work), so C3 containment holds no matter the caller. The guard honors the SAME `LAZY_ORCHESTRATOR=1` immunity signal every other guarded op uses — the real orchestrator (whose CLI wrappers export it) is byte-unchanged (a harmless idempotent double-call: wrapper-then-library), while a subagent's DIRECT library call now refuses with exit 3 and zero side effects. In-process test callers run with no marker + no subagent env → silent no-op. Added two registered regression tests (`_TESTS`): (a) `test_apply_pseudo_direct_call_refused_under_cycle_marker_without_orchestrator` — direct `__mark_complete__` under a live cycle marker WITHOUT `LAZY_ORCHESTRATOR` → exit 3, no COMPLETED.md, SPEC status + VALIDATED.md untouched; (b) `test_apply_pseudo_direct_call_allowed_with_orchestrator_env_under_marker` — the SAME call WITH `LAZY_ORCHESTRATOR=1` completes and writes COMPLETED.md. Commit: fbc4f0e.
  - **GAP 2 DECLINED (gate-weakening — Prohibition #2):** the evidence's second fix hypothesis — exempt canonical `<!-- verification-only -->` rows from `apply_pseudo`'s ticked-box coherence requirement so an all-verification-only remainder completes WITHOUT ticking — was investigated and NOT implemented. A legitimate all-verification-only completion path ALREADY exists: `evaluate_completion_evidence` (`lazy_core.py:2316`) accepts a `result: partial` MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md whose `observation_gap_exemptions` block is populated with per-entry `spec_class` provenance, and `autotick_verification_rows` (`lazy_core.py:2619`) then ticks the certified rows under a cardinality lock (rows-to-tick > pass_count → abort). The evidence's "11 rows vs 3 assertions deadlock" is that cardinality lock CORRECTLY refusing over-relaxed/forged evidence — precisely the over-completion that let the subagent go rogue. `test_apply_pseudo_coherence_refuses_unchecked_verification_row` (`test_lazy_core.py:5710`) already locks the intentional "unchecked verification row at completion → refuse" contract; the proposed exemption would reverse it and require deleting a passing gate test. Declined as a gate-weakening move. (Also per evidence NOTE: the subagent's separate `remaining_unchecked_are_verification_only` zero-unchecked claim is a documented-intentional behavior, left untouched.)

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — fix is structural (a containment-guard call at the sole-author library boundary), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip). The specific class — C3 cycle-containment bypass via a direct library import side-door around a CLI-only guard — has NOT recurred: Round 20 (2026-06) added CLI-side `refuse_if_cycle_active` fixtures but never touched the library boundary, so this is the first round on the library-side hole (signal 2 does not trip). No near-neighbor side-door self-flagged — all completion-authoring paths route through `apply_pseudo`, which is now guarded (signal 3). No repeated deterministic dance (signal 4). Healthy structural fix.

**Pre-existing failures (NOT caused by this round):**
  - `test_archive_fixed_real_drivers_pass_audit` fails on the CLEAN tree (verified via `git stash` → 843/844, then `stash pop`): a merged-view parity audit ERROR reading `repos/algobooth/.claude/skills/lazy-batch-cloud/SKILL.md` — that `repos/algobooth/.claude/skills/` tree does not exist in this checkout (not git-tracked here; provided by the skill-projection/symlink setup). Identical to Round 1's pre-existing note. Unrelated to `apply_pseudo`; not touched by this fix.
  - `lint-skills.py`: 1 `planner-resolution` warning (`write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`) — same missing tree, exit 0. Pre-existing, unrelated.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 845/846 (1 pre-existing unrelated failure — `test_archive_fixed_real_drivers_pass_audit`, confirmed via git stash; both new regression tests pass; orphan/dead-coverage guard passes)
  test_hooks.py: 107/107
  lint-skills.py: OK (exit 0; 1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK

## Round 3 — 2026-07-04 — process-friction

**Item in flight:** skip-mcp-test-frontmatter-unquoted-colon

**Divergence point:** the `/execute-plan` cycle's `--cycle-begin` dispatch bracket (bug pipeline). `bug-state.py --cycle-begin` was invoked for the preceding `/execute-plan` cycle WITHOUT `--sub-skill execute-plan`, so the cycle marker recorded `sub_skill=None`. At `--cycle-end`, `cycle_end_friction_check → detect_cycle_bracket_friction` derived the commit budget for `None` (the single-commit default `_CYCLE_COMMIT_BUDGET_DEFAULT = 1`) instead of the multi-commit ceiling `_CYCLE_COMMIT_MULTI = 3` that `execute-plan` (a `_MULTI_COMMIT_DISPATCH_SKILLS` member) would have received. `/execute-plan` legitimately landed 3 per-batch cloud commits (the sanctioned per-WU push discipline), which exceeded the mis-derived budget of 1 → a FALSE-POSITIVE `unexpected-commits` `kind: process-friction` ledger entry. Denial verbatim: `HEAD advanced 3 commits since --cycle-begin (begin_head_sha=f9e30b7ab1f6, sub_skill=None, budget=1)`. Probe: `step=Step 9: cloud defers MCP test sub_skill=__write_deferred_non_cloud__ feature_id=skip-mcp-test-frontmatter-unquoted-colon pending_hardening=1`. Registry: 7 entries, 7 unconsumed.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `detect_cycle_bracket_friction` (`lazy_core.py`) applied the single-commit DEFAULT budget to a `kind: real` marker whose `sub_skill` was never recorded. A real cycle with no recorded dispatch identity is BUDGET-INDETERMINATE: the multi-commit ceiling that distinguishes legit-multi-commit from runaway cannot be derived, so applying the default of 1 false-positives EVERY legitimately multi-commit real cycle. The detector already fails OPEN on every other under-specified input (null `begin_head_sha`, null `commits_since`, and `kind==meta` all return `None`, "a degraded input yields None signals, never a false positive") — but the falsy-`sub_skill`-on-a-real-cycle case was the one degraded input left to trip. The orchestrator prose (`lazy-batch`/`lazy-bug-batch` §1d) DOES mandate `--sub-skill` on every real `--cycle-begin`; this friction is that LLM-inferred contract being missed in a cloud run, with no script-side backstop.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: in `detect_cycle_bracket_friction`'s signal-(b) budget-derivation, when there is no positive `budget_override` AND `sub_skill` is falsy, disable the `unexpected-commits` signal (`return None`) — the same fail-open posture as the `kind==meta` exemption and the null-HEAD/null-commits guards. The integrity signals (a) cycle-bracket-break and (a.5) branch-divergence are evaluated ABOVE this block and are `sub_skill`-independent, so they still fire; a genuine runaway with a RECORDED `sub_skill` still trips (budget derivable). Docstring updated in lockstep. Updated the meta-exemption test's real-cycle control (`test_detect_friction_meta_cycle_exempt_from_unexpected_commits`): a real cycle with an unrecorded `sub_skill` no longer trips (indeterminate → fail-open), a real cycle with a RECORDED single-commit skill + 9 commits still trips, plus an explicit regression assertion for the observed instance. No coupled-pair script mirror owed — the fix is in the shared `lazy_core` helper both pipelines call. Commit: d650926.

**Over-fit spin-off:** harden(spinoff): class recurred ≥2, non-phrase (signal 2) → front-enqueue `/spec-bug` `cycle-begin-real-requires-sub-skill` for the class «the WRITE side: `--cycle-begin --kind real` structurally permits a marker with no `sub_skill`, so the commit-budget input is allowed to be indeterminate at the source». Cited instances: the `sub_skill=None → default-budget-1 → false-positive unexpected-commits` class in `lazy_core.py:detect_cycle_bracket_friction`/`cycle_end_friction_check` was hit in Round 15 (execute-plan, prose+budget-row), Round 16 (`__mark_complete__` meta-dispatch, ambiguous-prose), Round 17 (verify), Round 19 (meta exemption, first structural read-side fix), and this Round 3 (real-cycle indeterminate exemption, second structural read-side fix). Every prior round patched the READ side; the durable structural fix is the write-side guarantee that a real cycle marker always carries its `sub_skill` (validate/require `--sub-skill` at `--cycle-begin` for `--kind real`; meta cycles legitimately carry null and stay exempt), so the read-side has nothing indeterminate to tolerate and signal-(b) coverage is not silently lost on a forgotten `--sub-skill`. Class boundary — IN: the `--cycle-begin` write-side sub_skill contract on both state scripts (coupled pair) + any smoke fixtures that omit it. OUT: the budget thresholds/ceilings, the `_MULTI_COMMIT_DISPATCH_SKILLS` registry-derivation class (already covered by the open `adhoc-derive-multi-commit-budget-from-dispatch-sites` bug), and the read-side guard shipped this round. NOTE: the sanctioned `bug-state.py --enqueue-adhoc --type bug` enqueue was C3-refused (exit 3, zero side effects — this hardening agent is a contained cycle subagent); the enqueue is deferred to the orchestrator and surfaced via PushNotification + the `spinoff` return field. The observed instance is already fixed, so the spin-off never blocks this run.

**Intervention record:** the additive `--record-intervention --id harden-2026-07-r3 --pipeline hardening` capture (target-signal `event:process-friction`, direction decrease) was C3-refused (exit 3, zero side effects — orchestrator-only; this agent is a contained subagent). Non-blocking per the skill; deferred to the orchestrator's end-of-run flush. The round itself stands.

**Pre-existing failures (NOT caused by this round):**
  - `test_lazy_core.py`: run as a script in this cloud checkout aborts on TWO pre-existing, change-independent artifacts — (1) a live C3 cycle-containment marker (this very item) makes the subprocess-based `apply_pseudo`/`__mark_*__`/`validated_from_results` tests refuse with `SystemExit: 3` (the marker-induced refusals the dispatch mandate flagged); (2) `test_ensure_runtime_production_restart_spawns_via_shell_on_windows_cold_boot` raises a POSIX `Skipped`, which subclasses `BaseException` and escapes the in-file harness's `except Exception`. Both are unrelated to `detect_cycle_bracket_friction`. Verified via a full `_TESTS` walk catching `BaseException` under `LAZY_ORCHESTRATOR=1`: identical profile with and without this change (`git stash` comparison) — 926 tests, 912 PASS / 1 SKIP / 13 `SystemExit:3` / 0 assertion failures on BOTH trees.
  - `lint-skills.py`: 1 `planner-resolution` finding (`write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/` — that tree is not in this checkout), exit 1. Pre-existing (confirmed on the stashed clean tree), unrelated.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 912/926 PASS, 1 SKIP, 13 pre-existing marker-induced SystemExit:3 (identical before/after via git stash; the modified detector test + new regression assertion PASS; orphan/dead-coverage guard passes)
  test_hooks.py: 128/129 (1 legitimate skip: test_pipe_tests_wsl), 0 failed
  lint-skills.py: 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (unrelated; present on stashed clean tree)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 4 — 2026-07-05 — validate-deny

**Item in flight:** community-sharing (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, session `7088d261`, Step 7a execute-plan, `pending_hardening=1` at dispatch time)

**Divergence point:** Step 7a (execute-plan cycle dispatch). The orchestrator took a registered `@@lazy-ref` by-reference cycle emission (`nonce=bfb238761cf84f9e9c656c9632f1b909`) and **hand-appended** an `--- ORCHESTRATOR CONTINUATION NOTE (a prior cycle abandoned mid-part) ---` paragraph to it before the `Agent` call. The append mutated the resolved bytes (`denied_sha12: c79d0eed4f8b`) away from the registered emission, so `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` → `lazy_guard.py` denied it with the ORDINARY corrective recipe (guard case 3, "miss / no matching entry": *"dispatch prompt not script-emitted this turn — re-run the Step 1a probe (`--emit-prompt`) and dispatch its `cycle_prompt` verbatim…"*). The deny withheld the forward route (`route_overridden_by: pending-hardening-debt`, probe `step=Step 7a: execute plan sub_skill=execute-plan feature_id=community-sharing pending_hardening=1`) and routed THIS script-emitted, registered hardening dispatch inline (locked decision 4).

**Root cause:** none for THIS round — **working-as-designed re-route of the hand-append / non-verbatim-prompt-reaching-the-guard class already mechanically hardened (Rounds 2 & 4, June) and exhaustively prose-specified.** The exact failure — appending a note onto an emitted prompt — is the canonical example in the Freshness rule (`lazy-batch/SKILL.md:657`: *"Hand-editing emitted text is the failure class this rule names: appending a note … all mutate the hash and trip the guard … The template's `--context key=value` slots are the ONLY sanctioned customization point"*), the "Never hand-append to `cycle_prompt`" rule (`:580`), and the `@@lazy-ref` by-reference mechanism (`:707` F2a / `:709` meta-by-reference: *"the guard rejects mismatched hashes, so an orchestrator that accidentally paraphrases the prompt gets denied"*). This is the `@@lazy-ref`-hand-append variant: the appended text mutated the *resolved* hash of a valid by-reference token. Forensic evidence (per-repo keyed state dir `~/.claude/state/37850b6e…/` — the `multi-repo-concurrent-runs` dir for the AlgoBooth run; the claude-config run lives in the separate keyed dir `853ac81e…` and did NOT contaminate this deny — Round-26 per-repo keying confirmed working):
- **Marker matches the probe:** `last_advance_state_key = [community-sharing, "Step 7a: execute plan", execute-plan]`, byte-matching the injected probe JSON.
- **The mutated nonce `bfb238761cf84f9e9c656c9632f1b909` IS a legitimately registered `@@lazy-ref` emission** (registry entry `prompt_sha256: 324a0a9329ca…`, `item_id: community-sharing`, `consumed: false`) — a registered by-reference route was available; the orchestrator appended to it instead of dispatching it clean.
- **The denied sha `c79d0eed4f8b` is ABSENT from every registry `prompt_sha256`** (0 matches across all 7 entries) — the hand-appended prompt was never registered (guard case 3). The live deny-ledger `prompt_head` (`"@@lazy-ref nonce=bfb238761cf84f9e9c656c9632f1b909\n\n--- ORCHESTRATOR CONTINUATION NOTE (a prior cycle abandoned mid-part) ---\nA previous execute-plan cycle on THIS same plan part (part-2, Phases 3–4) d…"`) is byte-identical to the injected denied-prompt summary, confirming it WAS the `@@lazy-ref` reference, hand-appended.
- **The withhold + reroute + ack machinery fired exactly as designed:** the deny appended ledger entry `c79d0eed4f8b` (`ts 1783251030.82`, `reason_head` = the canonical corrective recipe, `acked: true`, `acked_ts 1783251088.65`); the probe WITHHELD the forward route over `pending_hardening=1` and produced the hardening route; the guard-allow of THIS dispatch (the IMMEDIATELY-following ledger entry `dispatch_by_reference: true`, `nonce 137d42860e37…`, `resolved_sha12 02316787d3c4`, `item_id community-sharing`; registry entry `consumed: true`; live cycle marker `sub_skill: hardening`, `kind: meta`) FIFO-acked the deny.
- **NOT depth-1 recursion:** the denied prompt was a non-hardening `execute-plan` `@@lazy-ref` cycle emission, so the guard returned the ordinary corrective recipe (not the depth-1 halt reason); THIS hardening dispatch is depth-0 and was allowed normally. Recursion depth stays at 1.
- Re-applying or inventing a fix here would re-investigate an already-hardened root cause (input rule) and risk weakening a correct, load-bearing gate (prohibition 2); a dedup-by-signature suppression would re-litigate locked decision 4 ("every occurrence is signal, not noise"). Mirrors the Round-27/29/30 (June) dispositions exactly — same non-verbatim-prompt class; this is the `@@lazy-ref`-hand-append variant.

Full gate suite run as health evidence (mandatory, to surface any latent defect) WITH the live AlgoBooth cycle marker present — all green, no new defect surfaced. Schemas untouched → coupled-pair mirroring + sentinel-schema lockstep N/A this round.

**Action:**
  - **No harness change.** The triggering misroute is the hand-append / non-verbatim-`@@lazy-ref` class already mechanically hardened (Rounds 2 & 4, June) and named verbatim in `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:657` (Freshness — "appending a note"), `:580` (Never hand-append), and `:707`/`:709` (`@@lazy-ref` by-reference guard). The deny → ledger-append → probe-withhold → hardening-reroute → guard-allow-ack machinery all behaved exactly as designed. Recording a mechanical fix or contract fork here would be dishonest (no new defect) and/or gate-weakening. Per-repo keying (Round-26 durable fix) confirmed working — this deny is NOT cross-repo contamination. Full gate suite run as health evidence (all green).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — no mechanical fix landed (working-as-designed disposition), so there is no fix to generalize; the durable structural fix for this class (verbatim-dispatch contract + `--context`-only customization channel + `@@lazy-ref` by-reference mechanism + Round 2/4 hardening) already exists. No over-fit smell tripped.

**Intervention record:** none — a no-harness-change round ships no intervention to measure (per the skill: additive `--record-intervention` capture is for the `Mechanical fix applied:` action form only).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 934/934 (orphan/dead-coverage guard passes)
  test_hooks.py: 129/129
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning — `write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`; that tree is not in this checkout, present every prior round)

## Round 5 — 2026-07-05 — no-route

**Item in flight:** community-sharing (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, Step 9 MCP gate)

**Divergence point:** Step 9 (the `mcp-test` sub-skill). The probe returned `step=Step 9: run MCP tests`, `sub_skill=mcp-test`, `feature_id=community-sharing`, `result=partial (observation-gap, loops)` — a no-route deadlock: an on-disk `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md` carrying `result: partial`, `pass_count=10`, `total_count=10`, and 3 `observation_gap_exemptions` (each with a non-empty `spec_class`) re-dispatched `/mcp-test` every cycle instead of routing forward to validation.

**Root cause:** `script-defect` — the Step-9 MCP routing in `lazy-state.py` (`~3381`, `if meta.get("result") == "all-passing"`) and its `bug-state.py` mirror (`~1489`) accepted ONLY `result == "all-passing"` before routing to `__write_validated_from_results__`. A sanctioned observation-gap partial (a feature whose behavior class is SPEC-LOCKED to the unit/WDIO test tier per `docs/features/mcp-testing/SPEC.md`, honestly carrying `result: partial` with a fully-passing MCP-driveable scope + `spec_class`-provenanced exemptions) fell through to `Step 9: run MCP tests` and re-emitted `mcp-test` forever. The two DOWNSTREAM gates ALREADY accept this disposition via duplicated inline predicates — the `__write_validated_from_results__` apply gate (`lazy_core.py:apply_pseudo`, formerly `~4202-4225`) and the completion-integrity gate `evaluate_completion_evidence` (`lazy_core.py`, formerly `~2934-2946`) — and the completion gate's own comment (`~2921-2933`) states it "MUST mirror the apply gate's promotion rule … to avoid perpetuating the deadlock one layer deeper." The Step-9 ROUTING was never given that same mirror, so the deadlock reappeared one layer UP. This is the same predicate-divergence class as Round 36 (June, the strict-`validated_commit == HEAD` equality that lived un-shared at the Step-9 freshness gate + apply gate) — an accept/promote rule duplicated inline across sites where one site diverged; the durable fix is a single shared home (the pattern `commit_drift_verdict` already established for the freshness carve-out).

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: extracted the observation-gap promotion predicate into a shared `lazy_core.observation_gap_promotable(meta) -> bool` helper (placed beside `commit_drift_verdict`, its structural precedent — the SINGLE-home pattern for a rule that must not diverge across sites). Routed ALL THREE sites through it: (1) the apply gate (`apply_pseudo`), (2) the completion-integrity gate (`evaluate_completion_evidence`), and (3) the Step-9 routing in BOTH `lazy-state.py` and `bug-state.py` (coupled-pair mirror). At the Step-9 sites the gate now accepts `result == "all-passing" OR observation_gap_promotable(meta)`; because the helper is HALF the AND (it does NOT read counts), the Step-9 sites additionally enforce the SAME `pass_count == total_count` cross-check the downstream gates apply (via `_coerce_evidence_count`), so a `partial` with a GENUINE MCP-scope failure (pass < total) still re-runs. The existing freshness / `commit_drift_verdict` gate is preserved unchanged for both dispositions (no gate weakened). Regression `test_observation_gap_promotable_shared_predicate` pins the shared predicate (the community-sharing live shape promotes; all-passing / no-exemptions / empty-list / provenance-less / whitespace-spec_class / non-dict-entry all refuse; a pass<total shape still returns True at the helper to lock that the count cross-check is the callers' half). Registered in `_TESTS`. Commit: `b2c0bc9`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL (extract a duplicated inline predicate into a single shared helper + route three sites through it), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip); and this specific class — observation-gap promotion predicate divergence at the Step-9 routing — is a first occurrence whose durable structural consolidation IS the fix (the healthy case). No over-fit smell tripped.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 935/935 (orphan/dead-coverage guard passes; +1 new regression)
  test_hooks.py: 129/129
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning — `write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`; that tree is not in this checkout, present every prior round; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 6 — 2026-07-06 — manual

**Item in flight:** recording-panel (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch 12`, retrospective harden pass; observed during the run's coherence-recovery cycles)

**Divergence point:** Step 9 (MCP gate) sentinel authoring. A corrective validation phase hand-wrote a `SKIP_MCP_TEST.md` intending to skip a SINGLE unvalidated verification row; the workstation Step-9 route (`lazy-state.py:3356-3378`) checks `skip_mcp_file.exists()` BEFORE `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md`, so ANY skip sentinel — regardless of authorial intent — routed the WHOLE feature to `__write_validated_from_skip__`, short-circuiting `/mcp-test` for the entire feature. Combined with a stale `VALIDATED.md` (which makes Step 9's `if not validated_file.exists()` skip the gate entirely → mark-complete refuses on incomplete phases), this produced an unroutable completion state that took 3 coherence-recovery cycles to reconcile.

**Root cause:** `ambiguous-prose` (sentinel schema) — `SKIP_MCP_TEST.md` is BY DESIGN a whole-feature, permanent waiver (schema: "un-testable on *any* host … never re-opened", `sentinel-frontmatter.md:110/163/429`). It has no row/phase scoping field, so it CANNOT express "skip one row." The sanctioned scoped-skip construct already exists and is fully wired — `observation_gap_exemptions:` on `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md` (`result: partial`, per-entry `spec_class`) promoted by the shared `lazy_core.observation_gap_promotable` gate (added Round 5). The routing behaved exactly as designed; the friction was a MISUSE of a feature-level sentinel for a scoped skip, and the schema did not explicitly forbid it. NOT a script defect — the `skip_waiver_refusal` provenance gate (`sentinel-frontmatter.md:447-451`) already refuses pipeline-self-granted skips; the residual gap was purely the missing "whole-feature only" scope statement that a hand-authoring path (coherence-recovery) tripped over.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added a prominent `SCOPE — whole-feature, permanent; there is NO row/phase scoping` note to the `SKIP_MCP_TEST.md` schema section in `sentinel-frontmatter.md`, directing scoped/partial skips to `observation_gap_exemptions` on `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md` and citing the recording-panel incident. Prose-only; no sentinel FIELD changed → no `check-docs-consistency.ts` `SENTINEL_SCHEMAS` lockstep owed (verified: required/optional field set byte-unchanged). Commit: `be91635`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is a structural scope clarification of an existing sentinel contract, not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip). The single-row-SKIP-misuse / SKIP-scope-confusion class is a FIRST occurrence in the hardening log (prior SKIP rounds — `skip-mcp-test-frontmatter-unquoted-colon` parsing, the `skip_waiver_refusal` provenance gate — are different classes; signal 2 does not trip). No narrow near-neighbor self-flagged (signal 3); no deterministic dance (signal 4). Healthy structural doc fix.

**Intervention record:** captured as `harden-2026-07-r6` — target-signal `undeclared` (a scope-clarification prose fix names no single measurable ledger event; the misuse manifested as a manual coherence-recovery loop, not a script-emitted deny/refusal). Degrades honestly to INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction per the skill. Non-blocking.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 931/935 (4 PRE-EXISTING failures — `test_lazy_state_test_output_matches_baseline`, `test_bug_state_test_output_matches_baseline`, `test_cycle_end_records_bracket_cli_lazy_state`, `test_cycle_end_records_bracket_cli_bug_state_parity` — verified via `git stash` of the two `.md` edits: all 4 reproduce identically on the CLEAN tree, introduced by the upstream 38-commit merge changing `--test` output + a subprocess/state-dir env dependency, NOT by these markdown-only edits; NO baseline regenerated per gate policy; orphan/dead-coverage guard passes)

## Round 7 — 2026-07-06 — manual

**Item in flight:** recording-panel (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch 12`; observed at the Phase-7 write-plan/execute-plan routing loop)

**Root cause:** `missing-contract` (authoring-side doc coverage) — the verification-row PLACEMENT RULE is exhaustively documented in `/write-plan` (`SKILL.md:117-121`) and `/spec-phases` (`SKILL.md:344`) and owned by the shared `phases-runtime-verification.md` component, but `/add-phase` — the very skill that authors corrective validation phases (the one authoring path that produces "run to PASS via /mcp-test" rows by construction) — referenced the component only for the gate-owned-row ban and reachability-smoke rules, never restating the verification-row marker mandate. So an `/add-phase` cycle could author an unmarked verification row and mis-route. The durable STRUCTURAL fix (marker-first detection) already shipped; this round closes the last authoring path that did not mandate the marker.

Mirrors the placement discipline `/write-plan` + `/spec-phases` already carry (coupled-doc lockstep across the phase-authoring skills). `/add-phase` is a standalone skill — not in the lazy-batch/lazy-bug-batch coupled pair — so no state-script mirror owed. Commit: `a6599a4`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix points `/add-phase` at the existing STRUCTURAL marker-first SSOT (it adds no phrase to any matcher — the detector is already marker-keyed, not free-text-keyed), so signal 1 does not trip. The broader verification-row-misroute class WAS discussed (Round 2 June GAP-2, declined as gate-weakening) and the structural marker-first detector already shipped (`harness-hardening-retro-fixes` Phase 2); this round is the completion of that structural fix's authoring-side coverage (the final skill that didn't restate it), not a recurring whack-a-mole patch (signal 2's "same root-cause class + same symbol recurring" does not apply — different component, and this is doc-coverage completion, not another detector patch). No narrow self-flag (signal 3); no deterministic dance (signal 4).

## Round 8 — 2026-07-06 — manual

**Item in flight:** recording-panel (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch 12`; two run observations dispositioned without a harness change)

**Divergence point:** (a) Step 9 (`mcp-test`) — a haiku mcp-test cycle FALSE-GREENED, narrating "all Runtime Verification rows ticked" when 0 were ticked on-disk and `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md` still read 2/2; the orchestrator caught it by on-disk verification and manually escalated to Sonnet. (b) AlgoBooth quality gate — `npm run qg -- ts` exited 0 despite TS strict-mode errors (a false-green in the target repo's gate).

**Root cause:** BOTH dispositioned WITHOUT a harden-harness change:
- **(a) haiku false-green → already hardened, working-as-designed post-rewrite.** The false-green occurred under the OLD prose-driven `/mcp-test` where the model self-judged assertions. That skill was rewritten to the **Informed Dispatcher** pattern (deterministic-runner Phase 8, landed in the 38-commit merge): a unit-tested TS engine (`scripts/mcp-test/run.ts`) evaluates every assertion IN CODE and writes both `verdict.json` AND the terminal sentinel; `reconcile-phases.ts` ticks rows mechanically. The model can no longer self-report a false-green — it doesn't judge or author the sentinel. Escalation off haiku is triple-covered: (1) the engine owns the verdict; (2) `route_mcp_test_tier` → sonnet on a legacy `.md`/no-candidate scenario, wired via `_mcp_test_cycle_model` (`lazy_core.py:6447`, called at `emit_cycle_prompt:6705`); (3) the loop-block flips model to sonnet UNCONDITIONALLY on a repeated signature (`lazy_core.py:6698`), so a non-definitive-verdict re-dispatch auto-escalates on the very next cycle — the orchestrator's manual override in the run was one cycle early, not a harness gap. Investigated the `route_mcp_test_tier(prior_verdict=…)` escalation condition (condition 2) not being passed by `_mcp_test_cycle_model`, but it is REDUNDANT with the loop-block's sonnet-flip for the re-dispatch case; wiring it would be a marginal duplicate, not a fix. Recording a mechanical change here would be dishonest (no live defect in the current harness) and risks the over-fit whack-a-mole the detector guards against. Mirrors Round 4's working-as-designed disposition.
- **(b) `npm run qg -- ts` false-green → OUT OF SCOPE (HARD Prohibition #1).** This is the AlgoBooth TARGET repo's quality-gate script (`scripts/quality-gate/`), not a claude-config harness component. `/harden-harness` works exclusively on `claude-config`; any path under the target repo's working tree is out of scope. Surfaced for an AlgoBooth `docs/bugs/` entry (the orchestrator/operator owns that enqueue) rather than baked here.

**Action:**
  - **No harness change.** (a) is the deterministic-runner rewrite's already-shipped structural fix (no live defect); (b) is a target-repo gate defect out of `/harden-harness`'s scope, surfaced for an AlgoBooth bug doc. Full gate suite run as health evidence (below) — no latent defect surfaced.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — no mechanical fix landed (both observations dispositioned without a harness change), so there is nothing to generalize.

## Round 9 — 2026-07-09 — validate-deny

**Item in flight:** key-detection-host-port (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, session `e3ee238d`, Step 7a execute-plan, `pending_hardening=1` at dispatch time)

**Divergence point:** Step 7a (execute-plan cycle). The registered `@@lazy-ref` execute-plan **cycle** prompt was dispatched by-reference and allowed normally (`nonce 6f9b4993…`, `resolved_sha12 749fadf668aa`, acked). Then a SECOND, separate `Agent` call — the cycle worker's `/execute-plan` **test-agent** sub-subagent (`prompt_head: "You are a TEST-WRITING agent (TDD) … You write FAILING tests plus the minimal module scaffold needed for them to COMPILE and fail at ru…"`, `denied_sha12: 3d662cb4514c`) — was DENIED by `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` → `lazy_guard.py` with the ordinary corrective recipe (guard case 3, "no matching entry"). The deny withheld the forward route (`route_overridden_by: pending-hardening-debt`) and routed THIS registered hardening dispatch inline (locked decision 4).

**Root cause:** `missing-contract` — the `workstation-recursive-subagent-dispatch` feature (commit `5ff570b`, 2026-07-09) lifted the workstation cycle-subagent inline-override ban so the dispatched skill's own sub-subagent model (here `/execute-plan`'s test-agent → impl-agent split) is authoritative again, and the emitted cycle prompt carries that authorization verbatim (`cycle-base-prompt.md` `@section workstation-dispatch`, lines 183–205). But `5ff570b` changed ONLY prose + `test_lazy_core.py` — it never touched `lazy_guard.py` or `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh`. The SPEC's guardrails (D3(a); prompt line 198) name only "the containment hook" as the mechanical backstop — the same-day `adhoc-containment-denies-mandated-explore-fanout` fix removed the *containment* hook's blanket recursive-dispatch deny — but the **dispatch guard is a distinct hook** that, under a live per-repo run marker, denies every `Agent` prompt that is not a registered emission or a resolvable `@@lazy-ref` (`lazy_guard.py:839` `_deny_default`). A cycle worker's test-agent prompt is worker-composed and cannot be a script-emitted registry entry (the state script has no knowledge of `/execute-plan`'s internal batch structure). The two hooks were conflated: the containment hook (operations) was fixed; the dispatch guard (prompt registration) was overlooked, so the FIRST workstation cycle to exercise the restored split had its test-writer denied. Session_id is not a discriminator — the sub-subagent shares the orchestrator session (`e3ee238d`), so the guard's session-mismatch fast-path could not distinguish worker from orchestrator (the deny confirms the marker matched). NOT depth-1 recursion: the denied prompt was a non-hardening execute-plan test-agent, so the ordinary recipe (not the depth-1 halt) was returned; THIS hardening dispatch is depth-0 and was allowed normally. The run is not hard-blocked — the worker's documented inline fallback lets it proceed — but the feature's core deliverable (the structural test-first agent separation) is silently defeated by the guard on every workstation `/execute-plan` / `/retro-feature` / Explore-fan-out cycle until resolved.

**Action:**
  - **NEEDS_INPUT.md written** (appended decision 4): `docs/specs/turn-routing-enforcement/NEEDS_INPUT.md`. Decision: "Dispatch-guard contract for WORKSTATION sub-subagent dispatches — how should `lazy_guard.py` distinguish a cycle worker's authorized test-agent/impl-agent split from an orchestrator improvising an unregistered cycle prompt, without weakening the integrity guard?" Options surfaced: (1 — Recommended) active-cycle-marker exemption scoped to sub-subagent-model skills, operator owns the cycle-marker-window fencing proof; (2) positive worker-set signal (env var / dispatch-depth); (3) register sub-subagent prompts via a new emit path; (4 — rejected) orchestrator-session-only scoping (session_id does not discriminate). No mechanical fix landed: the only mechanical change would loosen a security-critical integrity guard's allow set, and without an operator-chosen discriminator that is gate-weakening (Prohibition #2) — so this gate-semantics fork is surfaced, not baked. Cross-reference: origin `workstation-recursive-subagent-dispatch` (5ff570b) addressed the containment hook but overlooked the dispatch guard, which is owned by `turn-routing-enforcement`. Schemas untouched → coupled-pair mirroring + sentinel-schema lockstep N/A. Full gate suite run as health evidence (all green; a NEEDS_INPUT round ships nothing to commit beyond this log + the NEEDS_INPUT append).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — no mechanical fix landed (contract fork surfaced via NEEDS_INPUT), so there is nothing to generalize. This is a first-occurrence missing-contract gap (a just-shipped feature's incomplete rollout), not a recurring class in the hardening log.

**Intervention record:** none — a NEEDS_INPUT round ships no intervention to measure (per the skill: additive `--record-intervention` capture is for the `Mechanical fix applied:` action form only).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 935/935 (0 failed; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass; no live-marker SystemExit:3 this run)
  test_hooks.py: 144/144
  lint-skills.py: 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (`write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`; that tree is not in this checkout — present every prior round; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 10 — 2026-07-10 — validate-deny

**Item in flight:** key-detection-host-port (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, session `e3ee238d`, Step 7a execute-plan, `pending_hardening=1` at dispatch time — the SAME item/session/step/probe as Round 9, one day later)

**Divergence point:** Step 7a (execute-plan cycle). A cycle worker's `/execute-plan` **test-agent** sub-subagent (`prompt_head: "You are a TEST-WRITING agent only. Do NOT write any implementation code, do NOT edit .capnp schema files, do NOT touch any file other than the ONE test you add below. Do NOT run git commit/git pu[sh]…"`) was DENIED by `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` → `lazy_guard.py` with the ordinary corrective recipe ("no matching entry"). The deny withheld the forward route (`route_overridden_by: pending-hardening-debt`) and routed THIS registered hardening dispatch inline. This is the SECOND validate-deny for the identical worker sub-subagent split in the same run.

**Root cause:** `missing-contract` (recurrence of Round 9) — the dispatch guard still has no contract for a workstation cycle worker's authorized test-agent/impl-agent split (`workstation-recursive-subagent-dispatch`, commit `5ff570b`, touched only prose + `test_lazy_core.py`; `lazy_guard.py`/`lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` were never taught the split). A worker-composed sub-subagent prompt cannot be a script-emitted registry entry (the state script has no knowledge of `/execute-plan`'s internal batch structure), so under a live per-repo marker the guard's `_deny_default` fires. The contract fork that fixes this is ALREADY OPEN and pending operator resolution: `NEEDS_INPUT.md` decision 4 ("Dispatch-guard contract for WORKSTATION sub-subagent dispatches", written Round 9), whose recommended option 1 (active-cycle-marker exemption scoped to sub-subagent-model skills) would eliminate the deny entirely. No new root cause — same class, same symbol (`lazy_guard.py:839` `_deny_default`), same session.

**New evidence (beyond Round 9) — why the run does not self-halt:** `pending_hardening=1` at this dispatch proves a SECOND unacked deny-ledger entry was written after Round 9's was FIFO-acked by its hardening emission — i.e. the run re-hit the identical wall on a later plan-part. Crucially, the step-level oscillation tripwire is **structurally immune** to this thrash: `update_repeat_counts`'s ORDERED-ADVANCE EXEMPTION (`lazy_core.py:5847-5850`) RESETS `step_count` to 1 whenever `sub_skill_args` advances while the step signature is unchanged — and its own comment names exactly this case ("a multi-part `/execute-plan` sequence part-1.md → part-2.md → … that legitimately stays on the SAME 'Step 7a: execute plan'"). So a multi-part execute-plan re-denies the test-agent and re-dispatches hardening ONCE PER PLAN-PART with the oscillation tripwire never firing. The thrash is therefore **bounded by plan length, not infinite**, and **does not hard-block** (Round 9's documented worker inline-fallback — "keep the same discipline manually: failing tests first" — still completes each part), but it produces one byte-identical hardening round per part until decision 4 is resolved. Round 9 characterized the run as "proceeds degraded"; this round adds the specific mechanism (per-part re-dispatch + tripwire-immunity) and confirms it via the second occurrence.

**Action:**
  - **No new harness change.** (a) No mechanical fix: the only mechanical change that stops the deny is a gate-semantics change to the security-critical integrity guard's allow set, which without an operator-chosen discriminator is gate-weakening (Prohibition #2) — Round 9 forensically established that `session_id` does not discriminate worker from orchestrator, so no obviously-safe mechanical signal exists. (b) No duplicate/new NEEDS_INPUT decision: the root-cause fork is already open as decision 4 and this is a pure recurrence — re-investigating the same root cause without a new *root cause* would be noise (skill Inputs §4). (c) No thrash-containment fork spun off: a general "halt/dedup a validate-deny that matches an already-open harden-harness NEEDS_INPUT decision" policy would override the LOCKED unbounded-no-dedup cadence (decision 4 of the enforcement SPEC — "each occurrence is signal, not noise"), and the thrash-containment CLASS has recurred only ONCE (this run), below the skill's ≥2-occurrence threshold for generalizing a non-phrase structural concern. Recorded as a WATCH item: if the same re-dispatch-thrash-against-an-open-fork pattern recurs on a DIFFERENT fork, spin off the general cadence-containment fork then. For now the disposition is to ESCALATE the priority of the already-open decision 4 (its resolution eliminates the deny, the ledger entries, and the thrash in one move). Full gate suite run below as health evidence — no latent defect surfaced. Schemas untouched → coupled-pair mirroring + sentinel-schema lockstep N/A. This round's only artifact is this log append (committed `harden(docs):`).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — no mechanical fix landed (recurrence of an already-surfaced contract fork), so there is nothing to generalize. The thrash-containment observation is held as a watch item (single occurrence, below the ≥2 non-phrase recurrence threshold), not spun off.

**Intervention record:** none — a no-harness-change / recurrence round ships no intervention to measure (per the skill: additive `--record-intervention` capture is for the `Mechanical fix applied:` action form only; mirrors Rounds 8 and 9).

## Round 16 — 2026-07-11 — validate-deny

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, session `1a627773`, Step 7a execute-plan; state dir `37850b6e…`; BATCH of 3 identical validate-deny records, `pending_hardening=3` at dispatch, withholding the forward route via `route_overridden_by: pending-hardening-debt`)

**Divergence point:** Step 7a (execute-plan cycle) → the cycle worker's `/execute-plan` **TEST-WRITING (TDD red-phase)** sub-subagent dispatches. Three worker-composed test-agent prompts (`prompt_head: "You are a TEST-WRITING agent (TDD red phase) for AlgoBooth…"`; denied `cc79c0a628d4`, `56035f5e4f05`, `92cd2e7c7213` at ts 1783753317/350/380, bracketing the by-reference cycle-worker dispatches `e7bb66b1…`/`3d36de4d…`) were DENIED by `lazy_guard.py`'s default corrective-recipe deny — even though the **workstation sub-subagent exemption (block 2b, shipped 2026-07-10 as the decision-4 resolution) exists and targets exactly this split.** The exemption did not fire.

**Root cause:** `script-defect` (a NEW class — NOT the Rounds 9→13 no-exemption `missing-contract` recurrence; the exemption now EXISTS but is mis-wired). The exemption's condition 4 CONSUMED FENCE is `emission_consumed_by_nonce(cycle.get("nonce"))` (`lazy_guard.py:855`), which matches ONLY when the cycle marker's `nonce` equals the cycle's REGISTERED emission nonce — always a `uuid4().hex` (32-char) from `register_emission` (`lazy_core.py:12260`). But `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:688` permitted `--cycle-begin --nonce` to be "reuse the registry nonce when present, **else any fresh hex**", and the orchestrator passed a fresh 16-char hex (live cycle marker: `nonce: "5d231628fb9d836f"`). Verified against the live registry: all 31 entries are 32-char, the worker emission `e7bb66b1…` is present + `consumed=True`, so had the fresh 16-char marker nonce been the emission nonce the fence would have opened — a 16-char nonce can NEVER match a 32-char registry nonce, so `emission_consumed_by_nonce` returns False unconditionally → the exemption was **dead-on-arrival in production**. The unit test masked it: `test_hooks.py::_arm_worker_in_flight` hard-codes `write_cycle_marker(nonce=entry["nonce"])`, i.e. `cycle.nonce == emission.nonce` — a false-green that production wiring never guaranteed. (Contributing: the `else any fresh hex` prose is `ambiguous-prose`, but the CORE defect is the missing write-side binding — a production-wiring gap in a shipped feature.) The recurrence pressure was real: the same run's deny ledger holds MULTIPLE already-acked TEST-WRITING batches (`3d662cb4`/`23c3dec1`, `01a83de2`/`bc0273a0`) — the exemption failed on every execute-plan cycle.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added `lazy_core.resolve_cycle_worker_nonce` and wired it into `write_cycle_marker` — for a **subagent-model cycle**, `--cycle-begin` now AUTO-BINDS the marker's stored nonce to this cycle's worker emission (the newest UNCONSUMED `class=="cycle"` registry entry, which the preceding `--emit-prompt` just registered), regardless of the orchestrator's `--nonce`. When the passed nonce already matches a registered emission (the design-intended reuse) OR no unconsumed cycle emission exists (meta/degraded), the passed nonce is preserved byte-identically. The precise guard fence is UNTOUCHED (the cycle marker `nonce` is read by exactly one consumer — `lazy_guard.py:855` — so the rebind has zero other blast radius) and the security window is preserved: the marker binds to an UNCONSUMED emission, so the fence stays closed in the pre-dispatch window and opens only after the guard-ALLOWed worker dispatch consumes it. Shared `write_cycle_marker` → auto-mirrors to the bug pipeline (`bug-state.py --cycle-begin` @ `bug-state.py:7105`). Prose: reframed `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:688` + `lazy-bug-batch/SKILL.md` nonce guidance to PREFER reuse and document the auto-bind (coupled-pair parity). Tests: `test_lazy_core` `resolve_cycle_worker_nonce_rebinds_fresh_hex` + `write_cycle_marker_rebinds_nonce_for_subagent_model`; `test_hooks` end-to-end `exemption_allows_fresh_cycle_nonce` (production-order regression: register → write marker with fresh hex → consume → guard ALLOWS). No sentinel schema touched (lockstep N/A). No gate weakened; no registry/marker edited. Commit: `e3f5702`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL (a write-side rebind that makes the exemption robust to ANY `--cycle-begin --nonce`, keyed on the general `subagent_model` predicate + the newest unconsumed cycle emission — NOT a literal phrase added to a matcher, so signal 1 N/A; NOT a skill-list, so no near-neighbor gap). This is the FIRST occurrence of the shipped-exemption-mis-wiring class (Rounds 9→13 were the DIFFERENT no-exemption `missing-contract` class at a different symbol `lazy_guard.py:839`), so the ≥2-occurrence non-phrase threshold for signals 2–4 is unmet. No spin-off manufactured.

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r16` (`event:gate-refusal`, expected decrease; signal-independence: independent — the rebind makes the sub-subagent exemption fire, so worker-composed `/execute-plan` + `/spec-phases` sub-subagent dispatches stop reaching the guard's default deny; the refusal signal this fix targets is emitted by the guard, not by the fix).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 941/941 (0 failed; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass — 2 new tests registered)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed — 1 new test registered)
  lint-skills.py: OK — 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (`write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`; that tree is not in this checkout — present every prior round; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 17 — 2026-07-11 — manual

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, Step 7a `/execute-plan` cycle, workstation-recursive-subagent-dispatch model)

**Divergence point:** Step 1d cycle → `/execute-plan`'s test-agent/impl-agent sub-subagent split. The parent cycle-subagent dispatched Sonnet test-agents, then BLOCKED waiting for them to report results back via `SendMessage` before dispatching impl-agents. Every child's `SendMessage` to the parent FAILED ("the general-purpose agent isn't reachable by that name"); the parent returned RESULTLESS mid-cycle ("waiting on the two resumed test agents before dispatching impl agents") and needed a manual orchestrator `SendMessage`-resume telling it to finish inline.

**Root cause:** `ambiguous-prose` — the WORKSTATION DISPATCH sub-subagent policy in the shared `user/skills/_components/lazy-batch-prompts/cycle-base-prompt.md` (§ "Sub-subagent dispatch policy (WORKSTATION DISPATCH — LOAD-BEARING)", lines 182–205 pre-fix) said "FOLLOW that model" and carried guardrails for terminal-stop, single-writer, and scope-containment, but NEVER specified the sub-subagent *execution* discipline: that an `Agent` dispatch is AWAITED synchronously and its result returned directly as the tool result, and that a child cannot reach its spawning parent by name. The platform delivers a child's final result to the awaiting parent directly (no message needed); a child→parent `SendMessage` channel does not exist (only `main`/orchestrator is reachable by name). The harness ALREADY knew SendMessage-resume is unavailable in this workstation environment — Step 1d.0 (`lazy-batch/SKILL.md:598`) states "SendMessage unavailable in this workstation environment" for the orchestrator↔subagent case — but that knowledge was never carried down to the parent↔child sub-subagent level, so the model chose an async-dispatch-then-block-on-message pattern the platform cannot service → deadlock. This is a genuine harness prose gap, NOT a platform limitation: the correct pattern (dispatch-and-await) is fully supported; the policy just failed to pin it.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added a SYNCHRONOUS AWAIT guardrail bullet to the WORKSTATION DISPATCH policy in the shared `cycle-base-prompt.md` component (single-source → auto-mirrors to feature + bug pipelines via `!cat`). It states: AWAIT each `Agent` dispatch and consume the child's returned result directly (no SendMessage ever needed to collect a child's work); a child CANNOT reach its spawning parent by name; NEVER dispatch children async and block on a child→parent message (that is a DEADLOCK → resultless mid-cycle return); sequence dependent children synchronously (test-agent AWAIT → consume failing tests → THEN impl-agent AWAIT); independent children may batch-dispatch but you still await returned results, never a message FROM them; "waiting for a sub-subagent's message" is NEVER a valid cycle state. Projections regenerated (`project-skills.py`: 88 skills / 97 components, no errors). No gate weakened; no registry/marker touched; no sentinel schema touched (lockstep N/A). Commit: `2caa0de`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL (a new execution-discipline guardrail reconciling the sub-subagent policy with the already-known "SendMessage unavailable" platform fact), NOT a literal phrase added to a matcher (signal 1 N/A). This is the FIRST occurrence of the sub-subagent-deadlock class at this symbol (the WORKSTATION DISPATCH policy, shipped 2026-07-09; Rounds 9→16 were guard-side `missing-contract`/`script-defect` at `lazy_guard.py`, a different symbol) — the ≥2-occurrence non-phrase threshold (signals 2–4) is unmet. Signal 3 refuted: the single guardrail covers both the dependent (sequenced) and independent (batched) child cases, so no near-neighbor gap remains.

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r17` (`target_signal: undeclared` — the sub-subagent deadlock manifests as a resultless mid-cycle return, not a claude-config deny-ledger event type, so no measurable ledger signal is declared; degrades honestly to INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction per the skill).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 941/941 (0 failed; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed)
  lint-skills.py: OK — 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (`write-plan-cognito` not resolvable under any `repos/*/.claude/skills/`; that tree is not in this checkout — present every prior round; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 18 — 2026-07-11 — manual

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, cycle dispatch)

**Divergence point:** Step 1d cycle dispatch → F2a dispatch-by-reference. A `cycle_prompt_ref` (`@@lazy-ref nonce=…`) taken from a hook-injected LAZY-ROUTE banner resolved to the BARE TOKEN on dispatch — the subagent received the literal string, took 0 tool uses, returned "no task attached." Same-turn self-probe refs (from a manual `--emit-prompt` probe in the same turn as dispatch) resolved every time; only the banner-sourced ref (registered by `lazy-route-inject.sh`'s probe, dispatched a turn later) failed.

**Root cause:** `hook-defect` + `ambiguous-prose` — `lazy_inject.py` surfaced a copyable `by-ref: @@lazy-ref nonce=<hex>` DISPATCH line in the banner (line 283 pre-fix), inviting dispatch by-reference straight from the banner. That is valid ONLY on the turn the banner is injected (the inject hook registers the emission on THIS turn's UserPromptSubmit — so `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:385` correctly says "consume the banner directly"). But a banner persists in context across turn boundaries, so the copyable line is a carryover hazard: dispatched a turn later it violates the Freshness rule (`lazy-batch/SKILL.md:665` "never dispatch an emission from an earlier turn") — by then the nonce is stale/consumed/superseded, so `resolve_emission_by_nonce` (`lazy_core.py:12493`, gates: unconsumed + TTL + `emitted_at >= run.started_at`) returns None and the guard's F2a cannot resolve it. A near-miss transcription (copying the token WITH the `by-ref:`/surrounding banner text) is not a bare-ref match (`_REF_RE = ^@@lazy-ref nonce=([0-9a-f]+)$`, `lazy_guard.py:77`), so under a session-diverged marker (`read_run_marker` path B → None) the `_is_bare_ref` deny (`lazy_guard.py:622`) does not fire and the literal token slips through the `marker is None → return None` allow to the subagent. The prose gap: `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:715` "use the probe's `cycle_prompt_ref`" never distinguished the banner ref from a same-turn `--emit-prompt` ref nor tied banner-ref use to the Freshness rule. Confirmed the banner `by-ref:` token has NO sanctioned consumer: the F2a consumer is the orchestrator's own same-turn probe ref (§1d:715), and `test_hooks.py::test_inject_emits_lazy_route_banner` asserts only banner-prefix + probe-evidence, never the `by-ref:` line.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: (a) `lazy_inject.py` — dropped the copyable `by-ref: @@lazy-ref` dispatch line; the nonce is now surfaced as EVIDENCE with an explicit same-turn/stale caveat (by-ref valid only the injecting turn; if a turn boundary intervened the banner is STALE → dispatch the banner's full `cycle_prompt` verbatim or re-probe). The banner already carries full `cycle_prompt` for same-turn verbatim dispatch, so the by-ref line was pure convenience — dropping it removes the hazard while the same-turn path keeps working. (b) `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:715` (F2a) — reconciled with (not contradicting) the §1d banner-consumption rule: a by-reference dispatch is dispatchable ONLY on the SAME turn its emission was registered; the banner is same-turn-fresh only the turn it is injected; a carried-over banner is STALE per the Freshness rule; when in doubt, dispatch `cycle_prompt` verbatim (always safe). (c) `lazy-bug-batch/SKILL.md` — compact mirror (coupled-pair parity). Projections regenerated. No gate weakened; the guard's existing bare-ref deny is untouched (remains the backstop). No sentinel schema touched (lockstep N/A). Commit: `3910c96`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL (removes the carryover foot-gun at its source + ties banner-ref use to the existing Freshness rule), NOT a literal phrase added to a matcher (signal 1 N/A — the guard's `_REF_RE` is deliberately left unchanged, since loosening it to catch near-miss shapes would over-match legitimate prose mentioning `@@lazy-ref` and risk denying valid dispatches). FIRST occurrence of the banner-ref-carryover class at this symbol (`lazy_inject.py` banner assembly); Rounds 9→16 were guard-side at `lazy_guard.py`, a different symbol — the ≥2-occurrence non-phrase threshold is unmet. Signal 3 refuted: dropping the copyable line + the Freshness reconciliation closes the class (no near-neighbor: the only other by-ref surfaces — meta-dispatch `dispatch_prompt_ref` and the orchestrator's own same-turn probe ref — are same-turn-emitted-and-dispatched by construction).

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r18` (`event:gate-refusal`, expected decrease; signal-independence: independent — removing the banner's copyable carry-over token and tying banner-ref use to the Freshness rule means stale banner refs stop reaching the guard, so the unresolved-`@@lazy-ref` deny + wasted-dispatch signal this fix targets is emitted by the guard/dispatch path, not by the fix).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 941/941 (0 failed; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed)
  lint-skills.py: OK — 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (as Round 17; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 19 — 2026-07-11 — manual

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, Step 7a `/execute-plan` cycle over `src-tauri`/`crates`)

**Divergence point:** Step 1d.0 runtime-ownership vs a later Step 1d `/execute-plan` build. Step 1d.0 boots the orchestrator-owned Tauri dev runtime for an `mcp-test` cycle and keeps it up for reuse; a later `/execute-plan` cycle that touches `src-tauri`/`crates` then failed its `cargo check`/tauri-build with `Os { code: 5, kind: PermissionDenied }` — the live `algobooth.exe`/sidecar holds a lock on `binaries\node-x86_64-pc-windows-msvc.exe` (the tauri `externalBin` copy target). Rust could not compile at all.

**Root cause:** `missing-contract` — a legitimately novel sequencing situation. The runtime-ownership lifecycle covered boot (Step 1d.0, `lazy-batch/SKILL.md:594`) and run-end teardown (§1c.6:482, `dev:kill`), but had NO rule for MID-RUN teardown before a Rust-building cycle. The kept-alive runtime (booted to validate feature/part A) holds the sidecar-binary lock that the tauri-build externalBin copy needs for feature/part B, and the `stale_binary`/`--ensure-runtime` staleness path only fires at the NEXT `mcp-test` cycle — never before an intervening `execute-plan` build. So the lock was never released at the boundary that needed it.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added Step 1d.0a to `lazy-batch/SKILL.md` (+ compact mirror in `lazy-bug-batch/SKILL.md`): for a `sub_skill ∈ {execute-plan, spec-phases}` cycle that may compile `src-tauri`/`crates` with an orchestrator-owned runtime up, run `npm run dev:kill` (no-op-safe when nothing is running) at the CYCLE BOUNDARY before dispatch to release the sidecar-binary lock; a later `mcp-test` cycle re-boots via Step 1d.0's `--ensure-runtime`, and a `src-tauri`/`crates` commit staleness-invalidates the runtime anyway, so nothing is lost. CRITICAL SAFETY encoded verbatim: teardown is a boundary op ONLY — NEVER `dev:kill` mid-Rust-link (documented 117-LNK-unresolved-externals corruption; fix is `cargo clean -p algobooth` + rebuild). No new `blocker_kind`, no script change, no gate weakened, no sentinel schema touched. Commit: `85f28cb`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is a new STRUCTURAL sequencing sub-step (a missing lifecycle rule), NOT a literal phrase added to a matcher (signal 1 N/A). FIRST occurrence of the kept-alive-runtime-vs-build class — no recurrence, so signals 2–4's ≥2 threshold is unmet.

**Follow-up (MINOR, recorded not fixed):** the marker `forward_cycles` lags true completed-cycle count (probe `cycle_header` showed "fwd 1" after 2 completed cycles, "fwd 2" after 5). This is the KNOWN `byref-dispatch-undercounts-forward-cycles` non-monotonic-oracle class: `advance_run_counters` (`lazy_core.py:13638`) gates on `consumed_emission_count()`, which decays as the registry ring-cap evicts consumed entries, so when several by-ref dispatches' consumes are absorbed by eviction between advances the census delta < the real dispatch count and the counter under-advances. Phase 2's clamp (`lazy_core.py:13712`) re-arms only ONCE per census-drop observation, so multi-consume-eviction still lags. A durable fix needs a persistent cumulative consume counter (incremented at consume time, never evicted) instead of a live-census oracle — a non-trivial change to the security-adjacent consume path already two phases deep. NOT low-risk → deliberately NOT fixed in this hardening round; recorded here as a follow-up against the existing `byref-dispatch-undercounts-forward-cycles` item rather than a duplicate spin-off.

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r19` (`target_signal: undeclared` — the build-lock manifests as an in-cycle `cargo`/tauri-build `PermissionDenied` failure inside the target repo, not a claude-config deny-ledger event type, so no measurable harness ledger signal is declared; degrades honestly to INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 941/941 (0 failed; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed)
  lint-skills.py: OK — 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (as Round 17; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 20 — 2026-07-11 — manual

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, Step 9 `/mcp-test` validation)

**Divergence point:** Step-9 MCP staleness routing (`mcp-test` re-verify vs Step 9b `__write_validated_from_results__`). A first-run `/mcp-test` cycle authored two live scenario `.yaml` files and committed them alongside `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md`; the next probe routed a SECOND full `mcp-test` re-verify cycle (~5 min, ~148k tokens, zero new validation signal), then the following probe accepted the docs-only-drift and proceeded. Two operator-visible gaps surfaced.

**Root cause:**
  - **GAP 1 (`script-defect`, FIXED):** `commit_drift_verdict` (`lazy_core.py:3192`) computed `non_docs = [p for p in changed if not p.lower().endswith(".md")]` — i.e. the "non-invalidating drift" carve-out (Round 36, 2026-06-23) accepted ONLY `*.md`. But an `/mcp-test` FIRST-RUN commits its newly-authored scenario `.yaml` (`docs/testing/mcp-tests/corpus/live/*.yaml`) in the SAME commit as `MCP_TEST_RESULTS.md`. Confirmed on the live commit `efd4fc9→0c6c8f18f`: two `.yaml` scenario files → `non_docs` non-empty → verdict `non-docs-drift` → Step-9 routing forced the wasted re-verify. The very next commit (`0c6c8f18f→6d95a283b`) touched only `.md` → `docs-only` → accepted, proving the `.yaml` was the sole cause. A scenario definition IS the test, never the code-under-test, so it cannot invalidate the validation — the carve-out was structurally too narrow.
  - **GAP 2 (design fork — NOT baked, ALREADY OPEN):** `observation_gap_promotable` (`lazy_core.py:3128`) promotes a `result: partial` when its DECLARED `observation_gap_exemptions` are well-formed (each a mapping with a non-empty `spec_class`) + `pass_count == total_count`. It never cross-checks that the declared exemptions COVER every open PHASES verification row, so a genuinely-uncovered, explicitly-non-exempt row is invisible: managed-llm-credits `PHASES.md:451` marks "Purchase CTA … genuinely untested, not an observation-gap exemption … has no ui_action coverage" and `:576` marks auto-refill toggle-persistence untested, yet `--apply-pseudo __write_validated_from_results__` minted `VALIDATED.md` (`result: validated-modulo-observation-gaps`) because the OTHER declared exemptions satisfied the predicate. This is precisely the ALREADY-OPEN operator decision in `docs/specs/turn-routing-enforcement/NEEDS_INPUT.md` decision #2 ("Partial-VALIDATED → `__mark_complete__`: route back to `mcp-test` when the PHASES verification matrix is incomplete, or change what mints VALIDATED.md?"). This round adds the managed-llm-credits instance as concrete reinforcing evidence; it is a gate-SEMANTICS change (broad blast radius across every feature's verification rows) and is deliberately NOT baked — it remains operator-owned.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied (GAP 1): added `_is_noninvalidating_drift_path(path)` to `lazy_core.py` — `*.md` OR `*.yaml`/`*.yml` under an `mcp-test`/`mcp-tests` path segment (case-insensitive, separator-normalized) → non-invalidating; product `config.yaml` / `.github/workflows/*.yml` (no mcp-test segment) still classify as invalidating TOCTOU drift. `commit_drift_verdict` now computes `non_docs` via this predicate; verdict string kept `"docs-only"` for call-site compatibility. Docstrings updated at the helper, the verdict enumeration, and the WHY paragraph. Not a gate-weakening: real source/script/product-config drift still refuses. Commit: `3b5e513`.
  - GAP 2: NO new sentinel written — it is already surfaced as `NEEDS_INPUT.md` decision #2 (harden Round 45). Cited here with fresh evidence rather than duplicated.

**Over-fit spin-off:** recorded, NOT front-enqueued (operator directed a halt-after-this-feature this run — a front-enqueued bug would sort ahead of the next feature and violate that directive). Smell signal 2 (class recurred on the SAME symbol): `commit_drift_verdict`'s non-invalidating-drift set has now been patched twice — Round 36 (`.md`-only) and this round (`+ scenario .yaml`). The durable generalization is a principled "is this changed path code-under-test?" classifier (product/source/script/product-config = invalidating; docs + test-scenario definitions + results/PHASES reconciliation = non-invalidating) replacing the accreting suffix/segment allow-list in `_is_noninvalidating_drift_path`. Class boundary: the drift classifier ONLY — NOT a broader validation-gate redesign (GAP 2 is the separate, already-open semantics fork). Cited instances: Round 36 (`.md`), Round 20 (`.yaml` scenario). To be front-enqueued as a `/spec-bug` on the next unconstrained harden pass.

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r20` (`target_signal: event:gate-refusal` — the fix removes a spurious Step-9 re-verify re-dispatch; expected direction: decrease in redundant mcp-test re-dispatches. Signal independence: mixed — the re-verify route is harness-emitted, but the wasted-cycle cost is externally observable).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 944/944 (0 failed; +3 new: `_is_noninvalidating_drift_path` unit + scenario-yaml docs-only + non-mcp-yaml still-non-docs; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed)
  lint-skills.py: OK — 1 pre-existing planner-resolution finding (`write-plan-cognito`, same as Rounds 17/19; unrelated to this script-only change; `--check-projected` + `--check-capabilities` both OK)
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 21 — 2026-07-11 — manual

**Item in flight:** managed-llm-credits (AlgoBooth `/lazy-batch`, Step 10 `__mark_complete__` Gate-1 coverage audit)

**Divergence point:** Gate-1 MCP-coverage audit (`gate_coverage` / `--gate-coverage`) refused `__mark_complete__` for a backend-heavy feature — `uncovered: ['#','D1'..'D9']`, `scenario_count: 0` — with TWO distinct defects.

**Root cause:**
  - **`script-defect` (parser):** `_parse_locked_decisions` skipped a header row only when the FIRST cell was `id`/`decision`, but the canonical SPEC table header is `| # | Decision | Choice | Source |` (first cell `#`). `#` slipped the skip → a PHANTOM decision `id='#', title='Decision'` that no scenario can ever cover → Gate 1 permanently unsatisfiable regardless of real coverage.
  - **`missing-contract` (no exemption path):** `gate_coverage` marked a decision covered ONLY via an `mcp-tests/*.md` scenario id/keyword match — it had NO exemption path at all. But mcp-coverage-audit.md's D7 disposition is "documented-MCP-untestable decisions get an inline SPEC test-exempt note." That note could not satisfy the DETERMINISTIC gate, so managed-llm-credits' D1–D9 (all backend/business-model decisions verified in the Cloudflare Workers/miniflare runtime, outside the Tauri MCP surface per PHASES `**MCP runtime:**`) were permanently `uncovered`. The prescribed resolution had no implementing code.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: (1) widened the header skip — first-cell tokens `#`/`no`/`num`/`idx` (+ existing `id`/`decision`) AND a structural check that the SECOND (Decision/title) column literally reads "Decision"; (2) added `_parse_mcp_coverage_exemptions` (parses a `## MCP Coverage Exemptions` SPEC H2 of `- <ID>: <rationale>` bullets, NON-EMPTY rationale required — mirrors the `observation_gap_exemptions` `spec_class` discipline so an empty stub cannot launder the gate) and wired it into `gate_coverage` (exempt id with rationale → NOT uncovered; entry carries `exempt: True` + `rationale` for audit; scenario coverage still wins). Not a gate-weakening: an exemption requires an explicit, rationale-bearing, human/agent-authored SPEC entry — the sanctioned D7 disposition, not a silent bypass. Commit: `dffa5d9`. Verified live: managed-llm-credits `--gate-coverage` went `['#','D1'..'D9']` → `[]` after the header fix removed `#` and the authored `## MCP Coverage Exemptions` section exempted D1–D9.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — although the header-skip added tokens to a matcher set (signal 1), the SAME fix ALSO added the STRUCTURAL title-column check (`cells[1] == "Decision"`), which IS the generalization the phrase-add would otherwise defer; and the exemption path is implementing an ALREADY-DOCUMENTED component contract (`missing-contract`), not fitting to observed data. First occurrence of both defect classes on this symbol — signals 2–4's ≥2 threshold unmet. Distinct from Round 20's `commit_drift_verdict` carve-out (different symbol, different class), so it does not compound Round 20's recorded over-fit note.

**Intervention record:** `harden-2026-07-r21` (`target_signal: event:gate-refusal` — the fix removes a class of spurious Gate-1 refusal on backend-heavy features; expected direction: decrease. Signal independence: mixed — Gate-1 refusal is harness-emitted, but the blocked-completion cost is externally observable).

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 947/947 (0 failed; +3: hash-header skip, exemption-parser rationale-required, gate_coverage honors-exemption; orphan + dead-coverage guards pass)
  test_hooks.py: 150/150 (0 skipped, 0 failed)
