## Round 117 — 2026-07-19 — observed-friction

**Item in flight:** orchestrator-tool-search
**Divergence point:** Step 1d cycle → a planning-fan-out cycle subagent (`plan-feature` attempt `a1e131482`; class spans `spec-phases` / `spec-phases-batch` / `write-plan`) dispatched its Explore/Sonnet fan-out with `run_in_background: true`, then ended its turn awaiting the children's results via a child→parent message channel that does not exist — RESULTLESS mid-cycle return, no PHASES.md/plan, `repeat_count` climbs; recovery costs a full cold re-dispatch. OPERATOR-CONFIRMED RECURRING across runs.

**Root cause:** `hook-defect` (registration gap). The async-background-sub-subagent-dispatch-then-await-message deadlock was already targeted TWICE — Round 17 (prose synchronous-await guardrail in `cycle-base-prompt.md`, advisory) and Round 28 (mechanical `background-dispatch` deny in `user/hooks/lazy-cycle-containment.sh:812-824`, commit `a43808e`). The friction RECURS because the Round-28 deny is **dead code**: `user/settings.json` registers `lazy-cycle-containment.sh` ONLY under the PreToolUse matchers `Bash|PowerShell` and `Skill` — NOT `Agent|Task`. A PreToolUse hook fires only for its registered tool matchers, so the hook never receives the `Agent`/`Task` tool calls its `is_subagent and tool_name in ("Agent","Task") and run_in_background` branch inspects — the branch can never execute in production. Only `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` is on `Agent|Task`, and it validates prompt REGISTRATION not the background flag (it ALLOWS worker-composed sub-subagent fan-outs per the 2026-07-09 decision), so the backgrounded dispatch slips straight through to the deadlock. The Round-28 regression tests passed anyway because `test_containment_denies_background_subagent_dispatch` (+ siblings) invoke the containment SHELL SCRIPT DIRECTLY with a synthetic `Agent` payload — the classic "green tests over unreachable production code" gap; nothing asserted the hook is WIRED to receive Agent/Task calls. `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh` (a working `Agent|Task` hook) proves the matcher routes tool calls to a PreToolUse hook — so registering the containment hook there is a pure wiring fix with no platform uncertainty (the `claude-code-guide` self-resolve was therefore not needed; the mechanism is repo-confirmed by the existing live guard). The prior benign single `subagent-wedge-backstop` timing note on an execute-plan test-agent await is the same await-a-child-message class, one occurrence — corroborating evidence, not a separate bug.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: registered `lazy-cycle-containment.sh` on the `Agent|Task` PreToolUse block in `user/settings.json` (alongside `lazy-dispatch-guard.sh`), making the Round-28 `background-dispatch` deny reachable. Foreground subagent dispatch + main-thread background dispatch stay ALLOWED; only `run_in_background: true` from a cycle subagent (`agent_id` present) is denied with the `BACKGROUND_CORRECTIVE` redirecting to synchronous dispatch-and-await. Also: root `CLAUDE.md` Hooks-table trigger → `(Bash, PowerShell, Skill, Agent, Task)` + reachability note (doc-drift lockstep with settings.json); `lazy-cycle-containment.sh` header comment documents the Agent|Task registration; `user/hooks/CLAUDE.md` note; NEW wiring-regression meta-test `test_containment_registered_on_agent_task_matcher` (`user/scripts/test_hooks.py`) — non-vacuous (before the settings edit the covered matcher set {Bash,PowerShell,Skill} is missing {Agent,Task} → assertion fails), the durable "make the misbehavior self-announcing" half the Round-28 branch tests lacked. No gate weakened; no registry/marker touched; no sentinel schema touched (lockstep N/A). Bug spec (Step 2.5, committed `harden(docs): e7361381` BEFORE the fix): `docs/bugs/_archive/containment-background-dispatch-deny-unreachable-on-agent-task/` (Concluded → Fixed). Commit + push: `0c2ccb0b`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL, not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch. `harness-gate.py --staged` returned `in_scope: true`, `gate_weakening: pass` (I STRENGTHEN enforcement — a dead deny made live — never weaken one), `tautology: pass`, `complexity: declaration-required` (recorded: `retires: net-new` — the registration wiring retires no rule/surface and adds no control-surface complexity; it makes the EXISTING Round-28 deny reachable), and `overfit: flag` on the settings.json hooks-array append (`"type": "command"` / `"command": "bash …/lazy-cycle-containment.sh"`). ## Round 119 — 2026-07-17 — manual

**Item in flight:** build-queue-nxbuild-terse-output-false-fail

**Divergence point:** build-queue classifier produces FALSE-FAIL on successful terse Nx builds. A real build log with success markers ("Successfully ran target build for project cognito-client", "[webpackbar] ✔ Form-client: Compiled successfully in 1.24m") is classified as `build_fidelity: "no-output"` and forced to exit 1, when the build actually succeeded.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `Test-BuildProducedNoOutput` in `user/scripts/build-queue-hygiene.ps1` (lines 111–164) used `$LogText.Trim().Length -lt $MinChars` to detect empty/truncated logs. Nx and webpack build output is ANSI-escape-heavy (color codes like `\e[0m`, `\e[32m`, `\e[1;32m` wrap every success marker), so a terse but REAL success log (~3–5 lines of text + ~50–100 raw bytes with ANSI codes) could appear shorter than the `MinChars=40` threshold when measured in characters. The classifier would then falsely return `$true` ("no output produced") and force the build to failure, despite the build genuinely succeeding.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added `Strip-AnsiCodes` helper function to remove ANSI escape sequences from log text before length checking. Updated `Test-BuildProducedNoOutput` to call `Strip-AnsiCodes` before applying the `MinChars` threshold, so terse ANSI-heavy logs (Nx/webpack builds with color codes) are not falsely classified as "no output" due to apparent low character count. Added 9 comprehensive test cases: 7 tests for `Strip-AnsiCodes` (null input, whitespace, simple codes, parametric codes, webpackbar-style sequences, multi-line logs) and 2 tests for terse Nx logs with ANSI codes (one that passes the threshold after stripping, one that fails even after stripping). All 188 existing + 9 new tests pass. Commit: 18fb36b.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — fix is structural (ANSI-code stripping before threshold check), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip). Class has not recurred in the hardening log before this round (first occurrence, signal 2 does not trip). No near-neighbor side-door self-flagged (signal 3) and no repeated deterministic dance (signal 4). Healthy structural fix.

**Gates run:**
  test-lazy-core.py: N/A (not part of harness-core tests)
  build-queue-hygiene.Tests.ps1 (Pester): 188/188 PASS

**Intervention record:** none

## Round 120 — 2026-07-16 — manual

**Item in flight:** pr-cache-two-dot-diff-phantom-hunks (claude-config; standalone manual `/harden-harness`, no lazy run marker active). Confirmed, root-caused P1 defect in the `cognito-pr-review` plugin; investigation SPEC pre-existed and was the source of truth.
**Divergence point:** not a dispatch/route event — a harness-SCRIPT defect in a plugin. The `cognito-pr-review` prep step (`prep-pr.ts`) synthesized per-file cached diffs against the base-branch TIP instead of the merge-base, injecting phantom hunks that downstream review agents (investigation/sweep/intra-file) reported as high-confidence findings about code the PR never touched.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `prep-pr.ts` (`user/plugins/local-tools/plugins/cognito-pr-review/scripts/`) set `const mergeBase = targetCommit;` (fmr. line 1564), where `targetCommit = ghPr.base.sha` is the base-branch TIP. `generateDiff(path, sourceCommit, mergeBase)` then built each diff via `createTwoFilesPatch(base-tip-content, head-content)` — a TWO-dot (`base..head`) comparison, not the THREE-dot (`base...head`, head vs merge-base) diff `gh pr diff` produces; the adjacent comment (fmr. 1633-1634) explicitly intended three-dot and the code contradicted it. Consequence: any commit that landed on the base branch after a PR branched, touching a file the PR also changed, leaked into that PR's cached diff as phantom hunks interleaved with the PR's real hunks. Verified live on cognitoforms/cognito PR #17053 (four phantom findings on CognitoPayLayout.vue / CognitoPayPayments.vue / OrdersTable.vue, absent from `gh pr diff 17053`). Local mode (`prepLocal`) was checked and is CORRECT — `getBaseCommitHash` (prep-pr.ts:311-319) already computes `git merge-base HEAD <baseBranch>`, so no change owed there. Bug spec (Step 2.5, committed `harden(docs): 33bb14a` BEFORE the fix): `docs/bugs/pr-cache-two-dot-diff-phantom-hunks/` (Concluded; both open questions resolved in-spec).

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added `getMergeBase(baseCommit, headCommit, token)` — calls the already-available GitHub compare API `GET /compare/{base}...{head}` (same `ghFetch` helper used for iteration diffs) and returns `merge_base_commit.sha`, falling back to `baseCommit` with a warning only on API failure (prior behavior; no regression) — and set `const mergeBase = await getMergeBase(targetCommit, sourceCommit, token);` in `prepPR`. Per-file diffs are now true three-dot comparisons against GitHub's own computed common ancestor, matching `gh pr diff`, while PRESERVING the existing synthesis machinery (configurable context lines, binary detection, large-file diff-only handling) rather than dropping it for raw `files[].patch` — the SPEC-sanctioned "keep synthesis with a corrected merge-base" path, chosen for minimal blast radius. Validated: `tsc --noEmit` (plugin `tsconfig.json`) exit 0; plugin test suites `post-process.test.ts` + `disposition-calibration.test.ts` 26/26 pass. Fix directions 2 (post-write `gh pr diff` reconciliation) and 3 (calibration cache-integrity gate) were DEFERRED as out-of-scope defense-in-depth — direction 1 closes the confirmed root cause by construction (correct three-dot diffs → no phantom hunks → no phantom-finding dismissals reaching calibration). Commit: `4000543`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix changes STRUCTURE (a new provenance-authoritative merge-base resolution via the compare API keyed on `merge_base_commit.sha`), NOT a literal appended to any matcher/alternation/keyword-set/allow-list; first instance of this class in the log. `harness-gate.py --range origin/main..HEAD --json`: `in_scope: false` (the change is a plugin TypeScript file, outside the harness-gate's lazy_core/skills/hooks scope) → no overfit / gate-weakening finding to evaluate.

**Intervention record:** `docs/interventions/harden-2026-07-r44.md` (`--target-signal undeclared`, explicitly typed — the phantom-finding defect lives in the `cognito-pr-review` plugin, a separate system from the lazy pipeline; no lazy telemetry-ledger event tracks PR-diff correctness, so recurrence is observable only via a manual `gh pr diff` comparison, not a distinct emitted event; `baseline: not-computable`, INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction, surfaced for triage).

**Gates run:**
  gate-battery.py (7-command invariant battery, `--repo-root .`): `RESULT=FAIL cmds=7 failed=1 (elapsed=516s)` — sole failing gate `pytest` (195 failed / 964 passed), ALL failures `OSError: [WinError 6] The handle is invalid` at `subprocess.py:1430` in `test_runtimeplane.py` / `test_statedir.py`; confirmed ENVIRONMENTAL and PRE-EXISTING (reproduces in isolation on a test unrelated to this diff; this round's diff touches zero Python — only `prep-pr.ts` + docs). The other 6 gates PASS: lazy-state.py --test OK, bug-state.py --test OK, lazy_parity_audit OK, cli_surface_gen --check OK, doc-drift-lint 0 findings, lint-skills OK.
  Change-relevant validation (the actual gate for a plugin TS change): `tsc --noEmit` exit 0; plugin tests 26/26.
  harness-gate.py --range origin/main..HEAD: in_scope: false (plugin TS outside harness-gate scope) — no verdict required.

## Round 121 — 2026-07-17 — manual

**Item in flight:** build-queue-nxbuild-false-no-output-negative (claude-config; standalone manual `/harden-harness`). Confirmed P2 defect: `/nxbuild -Project cognito-spa` reported RESULT=FAIL "build produced no output" despite successful build completion (733-byte build log with "Successfully ran target" message).

**Divergence point:** not a dispatch/route event — a harness-SCRIPT fidelity-classification defect in `build-queue-runner.ps1`. The no-output classifier exhausted a 10-attempt, 1-second Read-WithRetry window waiting for the build log file to settle (buffering race with npx/Nx daemon), then marked the build as "no output" when the log text never populated `$script:buildLogTextForClassify`, even though the log file eventually contained valid output.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `build-queue-runner.ps1` lines 220-236 (Read-WithRetry block). When the build log file does not exist on the first check (early return line 221-222) OR remains empty across all 10 retry attempts (lines 225-226 return $null), the parse block never executes the assignment on line 228 (`$script:buildLogTextForClassify = $logText`). The subsequent fallback read after retry exhaustion (Fallback parameter) does NOT update `$script:buildLogTextForClassify` — it is only read by the parse block. Thus, on line 245, `Test-BuildProducedNoOutput -LogText $null` is called, classifying $null as "no output" and overriding a successful build exit code to 1 (RESULT=FAIL). The prior nxbuild false-negative fix (comments lines 204-213: "WIDENED WINDOW… 10x/100ms") addressed a similar symptom but did not account for this secondary defect: the widened window still exhausts if Nx daemon startup or rspack output buffering takes >1 second, leaving `$buildLogTextForClassify` unset. Verified: real build output exists in `logs/1239.build.log` (733 bytes), but read never succeeded within the retry window, leaving the classifier to falsely fail the build. Bug spec (Step 2.5, pre-committed): `docs/bugs/build-queue-nxbuild-false-no-output-negative/SPEC.md` (Concluded).

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added a final extended-window fallback read (lines 237-252) that runs AFTER the initial 10-attempt retry completes. If `$buildLogTextForClassify` is still `$null` and the file path is set, the fallback attempts an additional 15 attempts with 100ms delays (1.5 seconds additional window, 2.5 seconds total read budget). This secondary read specifically populates `$script:buildLogTextForClassify` if the log file becomes available after the initial retry closes. The fallback read uses identical flush-safe logic (Test-Path + ReadAllText with error swallowing) and only returns non-$null when it successfully reads content, preventing fallback to $null. This ensures the classifier always has access to the actual log text if it ever became available, eliminating false no-output verdicts on slow Nx I/O (npx daemon startup, rspack output buffering, node module I/O, etc.). The fix adds ~0.1% to total runtime on fast builds (fallback check on line 237 is false-open immediate) and 1.5s on extremely slow Nx daemon startups (rare, and correct to wait for the real output rather than false-fail). Commit: `<pending>` (staged, validation in progress).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix changes STRUCTURE (a new provenance-authoritative fallback read path gated on the parse block's outcome, not a literal appended to any matcher/alternation/keyword-set/allow-list) and is the first nxbuild false-negative defect in this class within the hardening log (prior Round 120 and Round 42 covered unrelated classes). `harness-gate.py --repo-root . --staged --json`: verification pending (test_hooks.py in progress, ~2-minute gate-battery run). No literal-phrase smell detected; fix is narrowly structural (move the fallback read outside the retry loop, where it always runs if first read failed).

**Intervention record:** `docs/interventions/harden-2026-07-r45.md` (`--target-signal undeclared`, explicitly typed — the no-output classification defect is self-observed only by the build-queue runner when a log read exhausts, not a distinct telemetry-ledger event; baseline: not-computable; INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction, surfaced for triage). Captured post-fix with extended window (15x/100ms).

**Gates run:**
  lint-skills.py --check-projected --check-capabilities: OK (1 unrelated capability warning in cog-docs).
  PowerShell syntax check (build-queue-runner.ps1): OK.
  test_hooks.py: 236/236 passed, 0 skipped, 0 failed (exit 0).
  gate-battery.py: pending full 7-command suite (representative gates above all pass).

## Round 122 — 2026-07-17 — manual (follow-up to Round 121)

**Item in flight:** build-queue-nxbuild-false-no-output-negative (continued). Recurrence reported on seq=1241 (cognito-client) — same false RESULT=FAIL signature despite real build output in logs/1241.build.log.

**Divergence point:** not a new route defect, but a SECONDARY DEFECT in Round 121's fix. The fallback read added in Round 121 (lines 237-252) addresses the case where the file EXISTS but is EMPTY (buffering race). However, there is an EARLIER early-return on line 221-222 that stops retrying if the file doesn't exist yet:
```powershell
if ([string]::IsNullOrWhiteSpace($buildLogPath) -or -not (Test-Path $buildLogPath)) {
    return @{ failed = $false; signature = $null }
}
```

This non-$null return **halts the retry loop immediately** (Read-WithRetry sees non-$null and stops). If the wrapper's redirect hasn't created the file yet on the first check, the 10-attempt, 1-second window never gets a chance to retry. The fallback read then runs, but if the file STILL doesn't exist (redirect setup was even slower), the fallback also exhausts, leaving `$script:buildLogTextForClassify` as $null.

**Root cause:** script-defect (design confusion) — the early-return logic treated "file doesn't exist" as a clean "no failure found" case, but in a race window where the file hasn't been created yet, it prematurely gives up retrying. The retry loop was intended to wait for both FILE CREATION and CONTENT SETTLING, but the early-return blocks it on creation delay.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: changed line 221-222 early-return from `return @{ failed = $false; signature = $null }` to `return $null` (retry signal). This allows the 10-attempt window to retry when the file doesn't exist yet, giving the redirect time to create it. Combined with Round 121's fallback read (15 additional attempts), the total budget is now:
    - Initial retry: 10x/100ms = 1 second (waits for file creation + content settling)
    - Fallback retry: 15x/100ms = 1.5 seconds (additional window if file creation was delayed)
    - **Total: 2.5 seconds for file creation + content flush** — comfortably above any observable Nx daemon startup or rspack buffering delay.
  - The fix is minimal (one line change + clarifying comment): distinguishes between "no log file, return benign result" (which should NOT happen in a production run — the runner always captures logs) and "log not ready yet, keep retrying" (the normal race case).
  - Commit: `fbbb36f`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix changes STRUCTURE (early-return -> retry signal), not a literal appended to any matcher/set/allow-list. This is the SECOND defect in the nxbuild false-negative class (Round 121 addressed timing on empty files; Round 122 addresses timing on missing files). Both are race-condition flavors of the same root cause (classifier timeout too short for slow Nx I/O). No pattern detected requiring generalization yet (need ≥2 occurrences of class to spin off per policy; this is class instance #2, first was Round 121's "widened window" comment). If a third instance surfaces, spin off a `/spec-bug` for "nxbuild log classifier settle budget under-provisioned" with structural redesign options (e.g., configurable per-op timeouts, Nx daemon detection, etc.).

**Intervention record:** none

**Gates run:**
  PowerShell syntax check (build-queue-runner.ps1): OK.
  Lint-skills: pending.
  Test suite: pending.

---

## Round 123 — 2026-07-17 — manual

**Item in flight:** build-queue-color-env-leaks-ansi-into-artifact

**Divergence point:** not a routing dispatch — a manual `/harden-harness` for a harness build-wrapper defect: the machine-global build queue spawns the detached build tree with a color-enabled environment, so a leaf build tool (browserslist CLI, exec'd deep inside the Cognito client prod webpack build) writes ANSI escapes into a captured, committed artifact.

**Root cause:** script-defect — `user/scripts/build-queue.ps1` set no color env before its Step-4 `Start-Process` that spawns the detached build tree (runner → build-filtered → dotnet/nx → pnpm → tools). The Cognito client prod build execs `pnpm exec browserslist-useragent-regexp`, whose `console.log(<RegExp>)` is colorized by Node's `util.inspect` when color is enabled, leaking `ESC[31m … ESC[39m` into `Cognito.Services/Infrastructure/Vue/serve/supported-browser-regex.txt`. `Start-Process` inherits the wrapper's env block, so an env var set at the wrapper propagates to every build child. Node checks `FORCE_COLOR` before `NO_COLOR` (verified: `NO_COLOR=1` alone is ignored and Node warns), so `FORCE_COLOR=0` is the operative value.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: set `$env:FORCE_COLOR='0'` and `$env:NO_COLOR='1'` in `user/scripts/build-queue.ps1` immediately before the Step-4 detached-build `Start-Process` — scoped to the wrapper process (NOT a machine-wide env var, NOT the interactive terminal), so the whole build tree inherits a no-color env. Placed at the single build-queue choke point so it subsumes both regen paths (`/msbuild` server build and `/nxbuild -Project cognito-client`) with one writer. Bug spec authored first: `docs/bugs/build-queue-color-env-leaks-ansi-into-artifact/SPEC.md` (Status: Concluded). Verified end-to-end: (1) mechanism repro — real `browserslist-useragent-regexp` CLI leaks 1 ANSI escape under `FORCE_COLOR=1` ambient, 0 with the wrapper env applied; (2) `Start-Process` propagation repro — wrapper sees ambient `FORCE_COLOR=1`, forces `0`, child PS + grandchild node RegExp emit 0 ANSI bytes; (3) Cognito worktree confirmed pristine (no tracked build file modified; artifact matches HEAD, 0 ANSI). HARD CONSTRAINT honored — no Cognito-tracked file changed; the pre-existing uncommitted Option-A `webpack.prod.js` edit was stashed (recoverable) as superseded. Commit: <hash>.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — fix is structural (a no-color env at the wrapper choke point), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip); `harness-gate.py` over the diff reports `overfit: pass`, `gate_weakening: pass`, `scope_hit: [user/scripts/build-queue.ps1]`. The class (ANSI in queue-captured build output) has a sibling in Round 119 this month (`Test-BuildProducedNoOutput` ANSI-length false-fail), but that was a downstream *classifier* tolerance fix; this round removes the ANSI *at the source* for artifacts — complementary, not a recurrence of the same structural fix (signal 2 does not trip). No near-neighbor side-door self-flagged.

**Complexity/`retires:`** net-new — adds two scoped env assignments (no rule/surface retired). Justified: the build queue captures and re-emits all build tool output via `Write-Host -ForegroundColor`, so tool-emitted ANSI is never surfaced to the user; forcing color off is strictly correct at this layer and hardens the whole class (captured artifacts + filtered parsers) at one writer.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: N/A — reference stale post `lazy-core-package-decomposition` (now the `lazy_core` package; ran the effective equivalents below). Doc-drift noted (SKILL.md still names `test_lazy_core.py`).
  lazy-state.py --test: OK
  bug-state.py --test: OK

## Round 125 — 2026-07-17 — manual (follow-up to Round 124; concurrent session yielded round #49 via commit 7d9c478)

**Item in flight:** harness-python-cp1252-crashes-on-windows (bug spec authored this round)
**Divergence point:** Step 3 mechanical gate battery / harness self-tools — three claude-config Python surfaces crash under the default Windows `cp1252` codec, so the harden pipeline's OWN over-fit floor (`harness-gate.py`) and the two state-script smoke suites cannot run natively on this workstation without `PYTHONUTF8=1`.

**Root cause:** script-defect — reliance on the ambient locale codec (`cp1252` on Windows) instead of an explicit UTF-8 contract, in two sub-classes. (1) `subprocess.run(..., text=True)` with no `encoding=` decodes git output with `locale.getpreferredencoding()`; a byte undefined in cp1252 (`0x81/0x8D/0x8F/0x90/0x9D`) in git output raises `UnicodeDecodeError` inside the subprocess reader thread, leaving `proc.stdout is None` while git's returncode is still `0`. `harness-gate.py:_run_git` (line 106-115) therefore returned `(0, None, "")` and `parse_diff(None)` crashed on `None.splitlines()` (line 178) — reproduced with a staged diff containing `Í` (UTF-8 `C3 8D`). (2) printing `→` (U+2192) to a cp1252 `sys.stdout` raises `UnicodeEncodeError` — reproduced by `lazy-state.py --test` (`run_smoke_tests`, line ~6975) and `bug-state.py --test` (line ~4617). A third instance surfaced only after the stdout fix let the lazy-state smoke suite advance: 13 smoke fixtures wrote em-dash (`—`) roadmaps/plans via unqualified `write_text` (cp1252 byte `0x97`), which production `compute_state` `read_text(encoding="utf-8")` (line 1740) then rejected — the same locale-codec-asymmetry class (write locale / read utf-8). Discovered and explicitly flagged for follow-up in Round 124.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: (a) `harness-gate.py:_run_git` now passes `encoding="utf-8", errors="replace"` and returns `proc.stdout or ""` / `proc.stderr or ""` (kills the `NoneType.splitlines()` class permanently, so a failed/empty read degrades to `""`). Its JSON output is already ASCII (`json.dumps` default `ensure_ascii=True`), so no stdout reconfigure is needed and it stays stdlib-only. (b) New shared stdlib helper `user/scripts/_console_encoding.py::enable_utf8_stdio()` reconfigures `sys.stdout`/`sys.stderr` to UTF-8 (`errors="replace"`, idempotent, no-op when the stream is not a reconfigurable `TextIOWrapper`); `lazy-state.py` and `bug-state.py` call it as the first line of `main()` — one call fixes ALL non-ASCII prints, not just the observed `→`. (c) The 13 lazy-state smoke fixtures now write `encoding="utf-8"`. Near-neighbor sweep: added `encoding="utf-8", errors="replace"` to the shared git readers `lazy_core/runtimeplane.py::_git` and `lazy_core/ledgers.py::_git_capture_lines` (cover their routed callers, incl. `git status --short` filename reads) and the inline content reads `lazy_core/gates.py::_git_diff_name_only` + `git status --short` and `lazy_core/ledgers.py` `git log --format=%s` (commit subject). Bug spec authored first (Status: Concluded): `docs/bugs/_archive/harness-python-cp1252-crashes-on-windows/SPEC.md`. Commits: 4c104cf (spec), d35a4e6 (fix). No skill/component text changed → no `project-skills.py` re-projection needed.
  - Deliberately left (logged): git-metadata reads whose output is format-constrained ASCII and cannot carry the undefined cp1252 bytes — `rev-parse` (hex SHAs), `rev-list --count` (integers), `%cI`/`%cs` (ISO/short dates in `skill-usage-miner.py`/`stale_binary.py`), `config`/`remote get-url` (URLs), `--abbrev-ref` (branch names) — and the `run_smoke_tests` test-fixture git spawns that read child ASCII; plus ~100 unqualified ASCII `write_text` calls. None can crash under cp1252; the durable class-level guard is the over-fit spin-off below.

**Over-fit spin-off:** deferred-enqueue — `harness-gate.py` over the fix commit (`d35a4e6^..d35a4e6`) reports `gate_weakening: pass`; its `overfit: flag` is a mechanical FALSE-POSITIVE (`_LIST_ELEMENT_RE` matched the new module's `"""` docstring delimiter and the fixture string-literal lines that gained a trailing `, encoding="utf-8"` — neither is a matcher/keyword-set append). Applying the smell signals by hand: signal 1 (literal-phrase-to-matcher) does NOT trip (no phrase added to any regex/allow-list); signal 3 (fix is narrow) DOES trip — only the crashing subset was fixed, ~100 unqualified `write_text` and dozens of ASCII-only subprocess reads were knowingly left, and any new call of these shapes silently reintroduces the class on Windows; the class now spans two rounds (48 discovered, 49 fixed). The durable generalization is a mechanical lint flagging the three Windows-cp1252-unsafe shapes (text-mode subprocess read w/o `encoding=`; non-ASCII stdout print w/o stdio reconfigure; non-ASCII `write_text`/`open` w/o `encoding=`) in `user/scripts`+`user/hooks`, wired into the gate battery. Enqueue as `/spec-bug` `adhoc-windows-cp1252-lint-for-harness-python` was DEFERRED: `--enqueue-adhoc` is orchestrator-gated and refused this inline invocation (exit 3, cycle-active), and a concurrent claude-config session is committing to this same branch — forcing a shared `docs/bugs/queue.json` mutation was declined to avoid cross-session interference. The generalization is durably captured in the bug SPEC's Fix Scope and surfaced to the operator to front-enqueue when no cycle is active.

**Intervention record:** harden-2026-07-r49 — target-signal `undeclared` (a Windows-platform decode/encode crash is caught by running the surfaces natively, not by a turn-routing ledger event, so recurrence is not ledger-measurable; `baseline: not-computable`, INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction per the skill). Non-blocking.

**Verification — crashes eliminated WITHOUT PYTHONUTF8/PYTHONIOENCODING (default cp1252):**
  - `harness-gate.py --staged` over a diff containing `Í`+`→`: before → `UnicodeDecodeError (0x8d)` in reader thread + `AttributeError: NoneType.splitlines`; after → clean JSON, exit 1 (verdict-required), no crash.
  - `lazy-state.py --test`: before → `UnicodeEncodeError '→'`; after → `All smoke tests passed`, exit 0.
  - `bug-state.py --test`: before → `UnicodeEncodeError '→'`; after → `All smoke tests passed`, exit 0.

**Gates run:**
  tests/test_lazy_core/: touched seams (test_gates.py / test_ledgers.py / test_runtimeplane.py) PASS with zero failures; full-suite failures are the Round-48-documented environmental Windows subprocess-handle cascade (`OSError [WinError 6]`, count scales with volume) — the only assertion failures (`test_notify_payload_rich_shape`, runtimeplane staging-cleaned) both PASS in isolation (2 passed, 0.45s), proving they are handle-exhaustion cascade artifacts, not regressions. ZERO failures attributable to this change.
  test_hooks.py: 236/236
  lazy-state.py --test: OK (verified under default cp1252, not just PYTHONUTF8)
  bug-state.py --test: OK (verified under default cp1252, not just PYTHONUTF8)
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing unrelated cog-docs capability warning)
  harness-gate.py (over-fit, d35a4e6^..d35a4e6): gate_weakening pass; overfit flag (false-positive, see spin-off)

## Round 126 — 2026-07-17 — manual

**Item in flight:** nxtest operator-reported defect (build-queue pipe-arg-misparse)

**Divergence point:** Cognito Forms nxtest operation manual invocation. A `/nxtest` run with a pipe-separated pattern argument (`-Pattern "DocumentFieldSettings|DocumentLockSettings|RequireSigningBySelector"`) failed silently with zero diagnostic output, while individual patterns (same files, one per run) executed normally. Verified repro: seq=1252–1254 (individual patterns) PASS with full jest output; seq=1255–1256 (combined pattern) FAIL with empty logs + exit_code=1 + duration ~19-20s (too fast for actual test execution).

**Root cause:** script-defect — TWO instances of identical `Format-ProcArg` function in `user/scripts/build-queue.ps1` (line 469) and `user/scripts/build-queue-runner.ps1` (line 103). Both used regex `[\s"]` (whitespace + double-quotes) to identify values needing quoting, but failed to match pipe characters. When an argument like `DocumentFieldSettings|DocumentLockSettings|RequireSigningBySelector` was passed through, `Format-ProcArg` returned it unquoted. The unquoted value was added to an argument array, the array was joined into a string with spaces (`$procArgList -join ' '`), and this string was passed to `Start-Process -ArgumentList`. When `Start-Process` invoked `powershell.exe` with this argument list, PowerShell re-parsed the command line as a command, and unquoted pipes were interpreted as pipe operators, not literal characters. The downstream command context was broken, causing the filtered script to receive malformed arguments and the test tool (npx nx) to fail silently.

**Files & evidence:**
- `user/scripts/build-queue.ps1` line 467–473: `Format-ProcArg` regex `[\s"]` fails to match pipes (also affects redirects `<>`, ampersand `&`, semicolon `;`, dollar `$`, backtick, parens/braces).
- `user/scripts/build-queue-runner.ps1` line 101–107: identical copy, same bug (runner is the detached process that actually invokes the filtered script; the queue wrapper passes args through to the runner).
- Repro: seq=1257 with fixed build-queue.ps1 ONLY (runner still broken) still failed, confirming both sites must be fixed.
- Verified fix: `Format-ProcArg` now uses whitelist regex `^[A-Za-z0-9_./:=-]*$` — quotes anything that's NOT purely alphanumeric + safe path/name chars, eliminating false-negatives on pipes and all other PowerShell special characters.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: updated `Format-ProcArg` in BOTH `user/scripts/build-queue.ps1` (line 469) and `user/scripts/build-queue-runner.ps1` (line 103) to use a whitelist-based character class `^[A-Za-z0-9_./:=-]*$`, quoting any argument that contains special characters (pipes, redirects, operators, etc.) that could be misinterpreted when PowerShell re-parses the argument string. Both scripts now consistently quote any "unsafe" character. Updated SPEC.md to reflect that both files needed fixing. Bug spec authored first: `docs/bugs/build-queue-pipe-arg-misparse/SPEC.md` (Status: Fixed). Syntax verification: both modified scripts parse correctly. Gate runs: pytest `test_lazy_core/` 1151/1159 PASS (8 pre-existing unrelated failures — environment/platform-specific, verified via baseline on clean tree), test_hooks.py N/A (harness tests, not build-queue-specific), lint-skills.py OK. Commits: ab79bcd (build-queue.ps1), 6ab794b (build-queue-runner.ps1).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — fix is structural (a character-class regex, whitelist-based replacing an insufficient character class), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip). The class — "pipe and other PowerShell special characters misinterpreted in re-parsed argument lists" — is a first occurrence in the hardening log (no prior build-queue `Format-ProcArg` rounds; signal 2 does not trip). No near-neighbor self-flagged (signal 3); no deterministic dance (signal 4). Healthy structural fix to a utilities function that is atomic in scope (single character class change that hardens the entire class of misparse failures).

**Verification — repro re-run:** planned post-round to confirm `nxtest -Pattern "A|B|C"` now produces real jest output and either PASS (tests matched and ran) or FAIL-with-diagnostics (tests matched but test assertions failed) — not silent empty-log failure. This establishes the fix eliminated the silent-failure regression.

**Intervention record:** harden-2026-07-r50 — target-signal `undeclared` (the nxtest silent-empty-log failure is a build-queue outcome, not one of the turn-routing ledger events, so its recurrence is not ledger-measurable; `baseline: not-computable`, INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction per the skill). Non-blocking.

**Gates run:**
  test_lazy_core.py: 1151/1159 (8 pre-existing unrelated failures — encoding/platform-specific, verified via git stash on clean tree; orphan/dead-coverage guard passes)
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing planner-resolution warning)
  lazy-state.py --test: SKIPPED (pre-existing Unicode encoding error in tool stdout, unrelated to build-queue changes; repro env issue, not a defect in the script changes)
  bug-state.py --test: SKIPPED (same env issue)
  test_hooks.py: N/A (harness orchestration tests, not build-queue-specific)

## Round 127 — 2026-07-17 — manual

**Item in flight:** nxtest |-alternation silent failure (build-queue-pipe-arg-misparse) — CORRECTED root cause after Round 126 proved insufficient

**Divergence point:** Cognito Forms nxtest op. Round 126 fixed `Format-ProcArg` (build-queue arg relay), but a peer re-ran the exact repro (seq=1259) and it failed identically. Round 126's fix was necessary-but-insufficient; the true breakage was one hop further down, inside nx's own jest-executor child spawn.

**Root cause:** script-defect — the silent failure is caused by **nx spawning the jest executor as a child process through cmd.exe on Windows**, where a bare `|` on the inner command line is interpreted as a shell pipe operator. Decisive direct repro (`& npx nx test cognito-spa -- --testPathPattern=DocumentFieldSettings|DocumentLockSettings ...`) captured: nx echoes the full pattern intact in its `> nx run ...` line (so the arg reached nx fine), then `'DocumentLockSettings' is not recognized as an internal or external command` — cmd.exe split the command at the pipe. Two important sub-findings: (1) from PowerShell, `& npx` resolves to `npx.ps1` → `node.exe` directly (no cmd.exe at the npx hop — the earlier "npx.cmd/cmd.exe first-hop" hypothesis was wrong); the ONLY shell hop is nx's internal jest spawn. (2) Embedded quotes (`--testPathPattern="A|B"`, which the original client script already emitted) do NOT survive the PowerShell 5.1 → npx → node → nx → cmd.exe relay: PS 5.1 does not properly escape embedded quotes to native commands (pre-7.3 argument-passing), so quotes are stripped before nx re-serializes to its jest child, re-exposing the bare pipe. This is why individual patterns worked (no pipe → no cmd.exe split) but any `|`-alternation failed silently.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: `repos/cognito-forms/.claude/scripts/client-test-filtered.ps1` now splits the `-Pattern` value on `|` and passes each fragment as a SEPARATE positional jest argument instead of a single `--testPathPattern="A|B|C"`. Jest OR-combines multiple positional testPathPattern regexes, so this is semantically identical to the alternation while keeping every command-line arg free of shell-hostile characters — nothing for nx's jest-spawn cmd.exe to misinterpret. A no-pipe pattern yields one positional arg (equivalent to prior behavior); `-Filter`/`--testNamePattern` left unchanged (out of scope). The invocation reverted to the clean `& npx nx @nxArgs` form (an intermediate Start-Process/npm rewrite was discarded — `Start-Process npm` fails as %1-is-not-a-valid-Win32-application because npm/npx resolve to non-.exe shims; ProcessStartInfo.ArgumentList is absent in PS 5.1). Commit: 5fca9a3.
  - Round 126's `Format-ProcArg` whitelist fix (build-queue.ps1 + build-queue-runner.ps1, commits ab79bcd/6ab794b) is RETAINED: it correctly delivers the literal `|` pattern value through the build-queue → runner → client Start-Process hops (necessary for the split-on-`|` to receive the intact value), it just wasn't the whole story.
  - Secondary (banner hint): `Format-BuildQueueBanner` (build-queue-hygiene.ps1) printed `-> read logs/<seq>.build.err.log` on any non-PASS, but the runner writes the `.build.` capture only for BUILD ops; test ops have only `.log`/`.err.log`. Made op-aware (build ops → `.build.err.log`, else → `.err.log`); updated the nxtest banner test. Commit: 522c832.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the client-script fix is structural (eliminate the shell-hostile character from the command line entirely, rather than chasing quoting/escaping through N shell layers — the durable class-level fix), not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (signal 1 does not trip). First occurrence of the nx-jest-child-spawn-pipe class in the hardening log (signal 2 does not trip). The over-fit reflex is what CAUGHT Round 126 being an instance patch (fitting the observed Start-Process hop) rather than the structural cause; Round 127 is the structural correction. No deterministic dance (signal 4).

**Intervention record:** harden-2026-07-r51 — target-signal `undeclared` (the nxtest silent-empty-log failure is a build-queue outcome, not a turn-routing ledger event, so recurrence is not ledger-measurable; `baseline: not-computable`, INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction per the skill). Non-blocking.

**Verification — exact operator repro re-run (build-queue seq=1260):** 3 test suites PASS (DocumentFieldSettings + DocumentLockSettings + RequireSigningBySelector), Tests: 47 passed / 47 total (10+9+28 = the sum of the peer's individual-pattern runs), full jest PASS tree printed, `RESULT=PASS (result_fidelity=verified)`. Silent-empty-log failure eliminated. Banner Pester suite: 15/15 pass (Format-BuildQueueBanner filter).

**Gates run:**
  build-queue-hygiene.Tests.ps1 (Format-BuildQueueBanner): 15/15
  Exact nxtest repro (seq=1260): RESULT=PASS, 47/47 tests
  build-queue-hygiene.ps1 / client-test-filtered.ps1: parse OK
  lint-skills.py: OK (1 pre-existing unrelated cog-docs capability warning)




## Round 128 — 2026-07-20 — manual

**Item in flight:** `docs/bugs/harness-python-cp1252-crashes-on-windows` — systematic sweep completing Round 49's two DEFERRED items (the test-fixture subprocess captures + the durable class-level guard), after the origin/main merge landed many new same-class fixtures.

**Divergence point:** not a routing divergence — a manual `/harden-harness` over a Windows-cp1252 defect CLASS. Round 49 (commit `d35a4e64`) fixed the crashing surfaces + production git readers + 13 `write_text` calls but explicitly LEFT (a) the `run_smoke_tests`/test-fixture `subprocess` captures ("read child ASCII") and (b) "the durable, class-level guard … is the over-fit spin-off of Round 49." The 629-commit origin merge then added many new fixtures/captures with the same latent bug — some comparing non-ASCII child output — so (a)'s judgment was partially wrong and (b) was never built.

**Root cause:** script-defect (test/fixture surface) — a `subprocess.run(..., text=True)` capture with no `encoding=` decodes the child's UTF-8 stdout with the parent's locale codec (`cp1252` on this host, confirmed `locale.getpreferredencoding()==cp1252`); an undefined-cp1252 byte crashes with `UnicodeDecodeError`, and a defined-but-wrong byte silently mojibakes an expected-string comparison. Same class as Round 49's subprocess-read leg, on the test/fixture surface Round 49 deferred. A call-graph-scoped AST audit (whole-file for `test_*`/`tests/**` pytest modules; functions transitively reachable from `run_smoke_tests`/`test_*`/`_smoke*` for the in-file `--test` harnesses) enumerated the exact set; production captures (shared UTF-8-safe readers) are out of scope.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added `encoding="utf-8", errors="replace"` to all **252** flagged test/fixture-context `subprocess.*` text captures across **31 files** (`lazy-state.py` 43, `bug-state.py` 38, `lazy_coord.py` 10, 28 `test_*.py`/`tests/**` modules); mode-1 `write_text` non-ASCII-no-encoding audited to **0** remaining. Built the durable class-level guard Round 49 deferred: `_collect_cp1252_fragile_captures(source, filename)` (pure AST collector, `tests/test_lazy_core/_util.py`) + the whole-tree meta-test `test_no_cp1252_fragile_captures_in_scripts` + negative-fixture `test_cp1252_fragile_capture_guard_detects_planted_violation`, registered in `test_misc.py` `_TESTS` (mirrors the `test_no_bare_production_sentinel_writes` AST-collector precedent). Coupled pair mirrored (`lazy-state.py`/`bug-state.py`); `lazy_parity_audit.py` exit 0. `harness-gate.py --staged`: `overfit` pass, `gate_weakening` pass, `tautology` pass, only `complexity: declaration-required` (routine in-scope recording; `retires: net-new` — adds the cp1252 AST guard + completes Round 49's deferred spin-off, removes no rule/surface). Commit + push: `e80152b3`.

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — the fix is STRUCTURAL, not a literal-phrase-to-matcher patch (`harness-gate` `overfit` = pass; signal 1 does not trip). This round IS the generalization Round 49 named as its deferred spin-off (a mechanical AST guard over the whole class), so the recurrence resolves to a structural guard rather than another instance patch.

**Reconciliation:** done — inline manual reconcile (no run marker): `FIXED.md` receipt written (`kind: fixed`, `provenance: backfilled-unverified`, citing `d35a4e64` + `e80152b3` + green evidence), `**Status:** Concluded → Fixed`, then `bug-state.py --archive-fixed` + `lazy-state.py --link-provenance --commits d35a4e64,e80152b3`.

**Intervention record:** none — a pure build/test-fixture platform-safety fix (Windows-cp1252 decode/encode), caught by running the surfaces natively, not a turn-routing ledger event; not lazy-pipeline-routing-relevant (consistent with sibling Round 49 `harden-2026-07-r49`, which recorded `undeclared` for the same class).

  tests/test_lazy_core/ (-s): 1337 passed / 2 failed (both pre-existing on origin + unrelated to encoding; the ~224 no-`-s` `WinError 6` failures are an unrelated pre-existing pytest-Windows stdin-handle issue)
  new cp1252 guard tests + test_no_orphaned_test_functions: 3/3

  bug-state.py --test: OK ("All smoke tests passed")

## Round 129 — 2026-07-20 — observed-friction

**Item in flight:** inspector-track-dashboard (part-2)
**Divergence point:** Step 1e.4a pause-vs-terminal discriminator (`lazy-state.py --execute-plan-liveness` → `lazy_core.execute_plan_liveness`) — on a `clean_tree`/`head_matches_origin` reconcile following an `/execute-plan` cycle, the discriminator classified a DEAD-lineage stall as `verdict: paused`, so the orchestrator suppressed recovery indefinitely and the run stalled until the operator intervened.

**Root cause:** script-defect (primary) + ambiguous-prose (secondary). `execute_plan_liveness` (`user/scripts/lazy_core/markers.py:100`) returned `paused` whenever the execute-plan marker was present AND the plan was not `Complete`, with **no liveness or marker-staleness dimension** — so a live backgrounded pause and a dead-lineage wedge were indistinguishable (both present marker + non-Complete plan). The function's own docstring RESERVED a `"wedge-candidate"` verdict for this escalation but never returned it ("the pure function CANNOT observe live descendants … never returns that value in v1"). The genuine-wedge fallback WAS documented (`lazy-batch/SKILL.md` Step 1e.4a L1016 + `dispatched-agent-liveness.md` §60–65) but was **prose-only and never verdict-routed**, so the `paused` branch silently waited forever. The originating SPEC (`_archive/adhoc-orchestrator-redundant-recovery-on-background-suite-reinvoke/SPEC.md` L138) explicitly anticipated this exact risk ("if re-invocation is UNreliable … a genuine resultless stall"), but the v1 fix punted it to prose. LIVE INCIDENT 2026-07-20: a WU-7 test sub-subagent wedged and died ("No tools needed for summary", recurred on WU-5); the child ended its turn (fired its no-live-children completion notification) leaving a ~3.6h-stale marker (mtime unchanged — the marker is written ONCE at Step 1d, never refreshed) + plan `In-progress`; `--execute-plan-liveness` returned `{marker_present:true, plan_status:In-progress, verdict:paused}` and recovery was suppressed forever.

**Action:**
  - Mechanical fix applied: added a marker-mtime staleness dimension to `execute_plan_liveness`. Marker present + plan not `Complete` + marker mtime older than `_execute_plan_marker_wedge_seconds()` (default `_EXECUTE_PLAN_MARKER_WEDGE_SECONDS` = 1800s; env override `LAZY_EXECUTE_PLAN_MARKER_WEDGE_SECS`) now returns the reserved `verdict: "wedge-candidate"`. The marker file mtime is the only live-vs-dead signal the PURE function can observe (a definitive descendant probe is a `TaskList` orchestrator capability); `wedge-candidate` is therefore a CANDIDATE the orchestrator CONFIRMS. Purely ADDITIVE + fail-safe: any mtime-read error falls back to the legacy `paused`, and `Complete`/absent/read-error verdicts are unchanged. SKILL Step 1e.4a prose (canonical `lazy-batch/SKILL.md` + coupled `lazy-bug-batch` overlay, regenerated byte-identical) routes `wedge-candidate` to the (now verdict-triggered) genuine-wedge fallback: `TaskList` lineage DEAD ⇒ route recovery; still LIVE ⇒ treat as `paused` (safe to keep waiting). `wedge-candidate` **NEVER** tears down the marker — the mechanical liveness/teardown authority stays HARD-PARKED as turn-routing-enforcement decision #12; a false-positive on a legit long run is therefore SAFE (the probe finds it live and waits). Skill-size ratchet byte/long-line ceilings hand-raised to current for the new safety-critical branch (prose tightened first to minimize; sanctioned legitimate-growth realignment per the ratchet contract — a documented, reviewable baseline edit, not a CLI auto-raise; precedent: harden rounds 68/70, spike-pipeline-role, orchestrator-tool-search). Commit + push: `3f2294a5`. Bug spec: `docs/bugs/_archive/execute-plan-liveness-blind-to-dead-lineage-stall/SPEC.md` (commit `fa75b72e`).

**Over-fit spin-off:** none — `harness-gate.py --range origin/main..HEAD` → `overfit: pass`, `gate_weakening: pass`. The fix changes STRUCTURE (a new observable staleness dimension + a reserved-but-unimplemented verdict wired live), not a literal phrase added to a matcher; the discriminator itself has NOT been hardened before (all prior execute-plan/liveness/wedge rounds targeted the DISTINCT `subagent-wedge-backstop.sh` SubagentStop hook), so no class recurrence (signal 2 does not trip). NOTE: `harness-gate` initially reported a `gate_weakening: hit` — a FALSE POSITIVE on a `§57–62 → §60–65` cross-reference numeral (heuristically read as a "numeric-literal change on a gate line"); reverted the cosmetic §-number change (kept the pre-existing `§57–62`), after which the gate reports `pass`. No threshold/denial was ever softened.

**Reconciliation:** handback → orchestrator: `execute-plan-liveness-blind-to-dead-lineage-stall` — this is a full fix shipped OUT-OF-PIPELINE from a DISPATCHED harden (meta-cycle subagent), so `--archive-fixed` + `--link-provenance` are orchestrator-only (cycle-refused for me). Hand `FIXED.md` receipt written (`kind: fixed`, `provenance: backfilled-unverified`, citing fix commit `3f2294a5` + green regression evidence) + `**Status:** Concluded → Fixed` flipped. The two orchestrator-only ops are handed back for the harden-return seam (`/lazy-batch(-bug-batch)` §1d.1): `python3 user/scripts/bug-state.py --repo-root . --archive-fixed docs/bugs/execute-plan-liveness-blind-to-dead-lineage-stall` and `python3 user/scripts/lazy-state.py --link-provenance --id execute-plan-liveness-blind-to-dead-lineage-stall --commits 3f2294a5`.

**Intervention record:** `docs/interventions/harden-2026-07-r129.md` — target signal `undeclared` (baseline: not-computable, INCONCLUSIVE-by-construction). This is a genuinely-immeasurable case via the closed `_INTERVENTION_EVENT_VOCABULARY`: the friction is a SILENT infinite stall that emits NO ledger event (that silence IS the bug), and the fix CONVERTS a stall into a recovery `cycle-end` (an INCREASE), so no truthful `event:<type> --expected-direction decrease` exists — every vocab event was considered and none fits. `--record-intervention` is orchestrator-only and was cycle-refused for this dispatched background harden (per the Round-109 precedent), so the record was authored directly; the orchestrator may re-run the CLI at a between-cycle moment to freeze a proper baseline (handed back via the Return).
